Also, Yang Xingqin has been assigned to other duties, and the resignations of Wu Rencang and Li Yuting were approved. All the vacancies will be filled by Hou Shenglin, Liang Xing, Huang Fangzhi, and Qin Yiwen. (7) Luo Xinjie was appointed Director of Education at the Guangdong Rehabilitation Institute. (8) The Central Supervisory Committee forwarded four cases of disciplinary action against party members: Yan Changxun, Chen Fangdu, Xie Guoyi, Ouyang Jiu, Xiong Keli, Tan Jutao, Chen Shuyuan, Gong Lichu, Zhang Yuanran, Liu Kezhi, Zeng Qingyi, Tang Shengjie, Hu Liangyi, Sheng Xianxue, Zhou Zixi, and Wang Kuiyi (Hunan) were permanently expelled from the party, a total of sixteen persons. Feng Renji (Feng Zhenhuan, Shandong Xintai), Huang Mian (Huang Heyuan, Hunan Yizhang), and Feng Anren (Shanxi Changzi) were expelled from the party, a total of three persons. Yu Tingyan (Jiangsu Qidong) was expelled from the party for three years. It was resolved that all shall be followed. (9) Commissioner Shao Yuanchong was recommended to report at next Monday's Central Memorial Week.

Central Propaganda Department Receives the Press 59

The Central Propaganda Department held a press conference in the Second Conference Hall of the Central Party Headquarters at 3:00 PM on the 21st, with over 20 reporters from various newspapers present. Chairman Zhang Tingxiu reported on three matters: (1) On the military front, progress on the Pinghan Railway has been rapid recently. Our forces have occupied Peicheng, west of Xuchang, and are currently advancing towards Gongxian. If Gongxian is occupied by our forces, the rear of Feng's army can be cut off. Feng's army on the Longhai Railway has gradually retreated since our army recovered Jinan. Although Feng's rebels are still trying to resist, they are not a cause for concern. As for Beijing, since Jinan was occupied by us, it has lost its last guarantee. However, the reactionary factions in Beijing, without any military certainty, are trying to quickly form a false government in order to deceive the public. This plan is not only impossible to realize but also extremely laughable. (2) Regarding public opinion in the North, recent investigations have shown that it is much clearer than before. However, there are still a few inaccurate observations. It is understandable that Beijing newspapers cannot speak freely under the oppression of warlords, but facts should not be erased. For example, after Jinan was recovered by the Central Government, a certain Tianjin newspaper, known for its neutrality, was vague in its language. This is truly disappointing. It is hoped that the press will faithfully represent public opinion in the future, and the Central Government will show sympathy and will not be overly critical. (3) The generals who recovered Jinan this time have made great achievements, and this victory is worthy of commemoration. Therefore, the Central Government has decided to send Commissioners Dai Jitao and Liu Jiwen to the front lines to express their condolences on behalf of the Central Government. The Central Propaganda Department has also printed a type of "Revolutionary Soldier's Diary" for the two Commissioners to take to the front lines and distribute to the officers and soldiers. After the report, the meeting was adjourned.

Shandong Provincial Party and Government Agencies Return to Jinan 60

Ge Jingen Travels West on the Same Train

Qingdao Correspondence: After Jinan was recovered by the Central Army, personnel from the Shandong Provincial Party and Government agencies who had remained in Qingdao began to prepare to return to Jinan. However, due to the impact of military operations on the Jiaoji Railway, it was difficult to fully repair it for a while. Therefore, two plans were drafted: one for sending advance personnel for takeover and one for full departure. Later, the plan has been changed several times without being able to be realized. Yesterday, according to news from the Jiaoji Railway, the remaining Jin army between Zhoucun and Zhangdian had completely withdrawn towards Qingcheng, and the Zibo River iron bridge was nearing completion. Light vehicles can pass through, so the provincial agencies decided to return to Jinan this (18th) evening. The Railway Bureau prepared a special train, consisting of five cars: a dining car No. 351, a first and second-class car No. 215, for the use of personnel from the Provincial Party and Government agencies, a car No. 601, for the use of personnel from the Jinan Arsenal, and two cars No. 623 and 223, for the use of all personnel from the General Headquarters. All personnel returning to Jinan were issued symbols by the Provincial Government for identification. Local Qingdao Party and Government agencies and various organizations will go to the station to see them off. Because there were too many people from various agencies, the original number of cars was not enough, so a third-class car was temporarily added. The train will depart west at 3:00 AM tonight.

Also, after receiving a telegram from Commander-in-Chief Chiang, Ge Jingen was instructed to go to Jinan when the National Army occupied Jinan to assist Commander Liu in handling important matters. Now that Jinan has been recovered, it is urgent to obey the order and go to Jinan. Therefore, he decided to travel west on the same train as the Provincial Government personnel. The Railway Bureau added a special car No. 106 and a third-class car No. 507 for Ge and his entourage to ride in. (August 18th)

Jiaoji Railway Prepares for Full Line Opening 61

Major Damage to Bridges, Telegraphs, and Telephones

Qingdao Correspondence: Since the Han and Jin armies fought along the Jiaoji Railway line, the entire line has been virtually converted into a military zone. Traffic was disrupted, and businesses, industries, and travelers suffered tremendous losses. The railway itself suffered property damage and operating losses, amounting to over two million yuan. Since the Central Army recovered Jinan, the entire Jiaoji Railway line has been under the control of the Central Army. In order to facilitate traffic, the Railway Bureau decided to step up work to restore full line operation in the near future. In addition to purchasing a large quantity of materials for emergency needs, today (18th) the heads of the Traffic, Engineering, and Locomotive departments were ordered to go to the line to supervise the staff, working day and night to speed up repairs. Unless there are unexpected obstacles, the full line can be opened within three days. The damage to the railway and the status of repairs are recorded as follows:

Regarding Bridges: There is no major damage from Qingdao to Zuoshan. The most serious damage is from Zuoshan to Zibo River. In between, bridges over the Wei River, Dawei River, Yun River, Zibo River, Xiaodan River, Baiyang River, and nearby small rivers have been damaged and blown up in varying numbers of spans. On the 12th of this month, the railway sent the heads of the Engineering and Traffic departments to inspect and supervise the repairs. Currently, the bridges over the Wei River, Dawei River, Yun River, and Baiyang River have all been temporarily supported by sleepers, allowing for barely passable traffic. The Zibo River Bridge is also under urgent repair, and is expected to be completed in a day or two. 10,000 sleepers have been transported there, but they are still not enough. Wood is being temporarily purchased in the city and transported for use. West of Xindian, there is less damage. Generally, once the Zibo River Bridge is repaired, the full line can be opened.

Regarding Vehicles: Since the outbreak of military conflict, about 200 vehicles in the western section have been detained by the Jin army. The eastern section currently has about 80 locomotives (including those from other railways), about 200 passenger cars, and about 1,400 freight cars. Most of them are now used for military transport. Those that have been damaged are being repaired. It is said that when the Jin army retreated, the Japanese intervened due to the railway's debt relationship, and the vehicles were not taken across the border. Currently, regular passenger trains have resumed operation (passengers must cross the Zibo River Bridge to change trains), running once a day in both directions. Freight cars can reach Qingzhou.

Telegraph and Telephone: Telegraph poles and generators at stations west of Zuoshan have been mostly destroyed. Even telephones and batteries have been taken away by the military. Repairs are being rushed, and priority is being given to repairing train dispatch telephones and route markers to meet emergency needs. However, there is a shortage of workers and materials. The existing ones are being used as much as possible, and workers and a large amount of materials are being borrowed from the local telephone bureau to facilitate the work. East of Weixian, repairs have been completed, and the rest will also be completed within the shortest possible time in order to allow for traffic.

Fundamental Repairs: The temporary repairs to the bridges are all made using wooden sleepers, which are a temporary expedient. The Engineering Department of the Railway has prepared detailed plans for fundamental repairs, and some sections are intended to be rebuilt with alternative lines, while others are temporarily using alternative lines. Steel beams and other materials are needed for the fundamental repairs of other bridges. In addition to the existing materials, those that have been purchased but not yet delivered have been telegraphed to urge prompt delivery.

Reduced Wages: The railway has suffered heavy losses in this war. The large quantities of materials used require huge sums of money. The salaries of the employees in the western section also need to be paid. The debt interest of 300,000 yuan also cannot be delayed. In the past month, traffic has been cut off, and operating income has only reached one-tenth of what it used to be. To prioritize the use of emergency materials, the salaries of all employees will be paid on a reduced scale. For those with salaries above 100 yuan, 80% will be paid first this month in order to make funds available. (August 18th)

Guangdong Northern Communist Bandits Recently Active 62

Zhu and Peng's Forces Split and Flee from Southern Jiangxi and Southern Hunan to Guangdong

Renhua County Magistrate Requests Troops, Nanxiong and Lechang Telegrams are Disrupted

Guangzhou Correspondence: Since the outbreak of the Communist rebellion in Changsha, Guangdong authorities have been thoroughly eliminating the remnants of the Communist bandits to maintain public order. Several months ago, the Communist Party organizations and criminal cases of Dongjiang Red Army Captains discovered in Sihou Street Datong Medical Society and Lao Jiaxiang in Guangzhou City, including multiple members of the Communist Party City Executive Committee, were detained in the Public Security Bureau. They were recently brought up for execution. All the detained Communists were executed in sequence. Those with lighter offenses were transferred to the Nantoutou Correctional Field Prison. In addition, the police have been executing inspections of firearms licenses every day to prevent bandits from infiltrating the urban areas. Therefore, public order in Guangzhou is still relatively stable. In the eastern part of Guangdong, Raoping County was previously captured by Communist bandits, but was retaken by a team from the 62nd Division stationed in the area at the beginning of this month. Currently, battalions and teams are tracking and suppressing the bandits. The Communist Party's General Office in Raoping has been raided, and several key figures have been arrested. According to a telegram from the commander of the 62nd Division, Raoping City was captured by bandits last month, and was recaptured by a special service battalion commander Huang Binglin. The commander reported in a telegram that the Communist bandits in Raoping, after being defeated by our battalion, quickly fled back to the Stone Well Bandit Nest and secretly plotted a riot. The commander led a team on a night raid on the (10th) day, killing over forty bandits on the spot, capturing seventy alive, including a head of the Communist Party, a propaganda officer, a Red Army platoon leader, a Red Guard Captain, and a secret communications officer (names omitted), who had been wanted by Raoping County. Also captured were a secretary of the false Raoping Soviet Government, a member of the Red Army children's corps, and a five-man squad leader, along with thirty-seven guns of various types, and Mi Yuchou, a clerk of the Raoping Branch Court, who had been kidnapped. A Raoping telegraph machine and many other reactionary publications were recovered. In the northern part of Guangdong, the bandit atmosphere has recently intensified. This is because the Communist bandits in Hunan and Jiangxi provinces have been suppressed, and Peng Dehuai's forces in Nanchang and Changsha have been unsuccessful, and have been gradually forced back by the Hunan and Jiangxi armies. Zhu and Peng's bandit armies have split and fled south. One force went to Ganzhou, fleeing to Xinfeng in southern Jiangxi, echoing the local bandits in Nanshi. Another force fled from Liuyang to Yongxing in southern Hunan, spreading to Guidong and Rucheng. Rucheng is adjacent to Renhua in northern Guangdong. The local Communist bandits in Renhua have also been stirring up trouble recently, threatening to attack the city. Therefore, the authorities dispatched guerrilla teams to deploy on the border yesterday. On the 13th, Renhua County Magistrate He sent a telegram of distress, saying that the Communist bandits in Hunan are fleeing south, causing panic in Yongxing County. The local Communist bandits in Xinfeng County, Jiangxi, have been unusually rampant in recent days, besieging the county seat. In order to protect the territory and secure the people, the magistrate has transferred all the police and soldiers in the county to develop the border and consolidate everything. The magistrate requested that troops be dispatched to the county to maintain stability. The authorities, after receiving the report, immediately ordered the 3rd Regiment of the Headquarters Training Corps, commanded by Wang Dinghua, to set off from the south on the 13th to the province. Led by Lieutenant Colonel Chen, the regiment supplemented its military equipment in the province and departed from Guangzhou on the Yuehan train to Shaoguan on the afternoon of the 14th to maintain stability. By the 16th, news from the local telegraph bureau was that telegrams in the northern parts of Guangdong Province in Renhua, Lechang, and Nanxiong were suddenly disrupted. It is thought that this was caused by the local Communist bandits sabotaging the telegraph poles. Based on this, the banditry in Northern Guangdong should not be underestimated. Therefore, the authorities are planning to dispatch heavy troops to suppress them thoroughly to eliminate the hidden danger. (August 17th)

Leather Merchants in Guangdong Oppose Excessive Tax Collection 63

Leather Tanning and Cattle Slaughtering Industries Unite in Shutdown

Leather Dealers from Guangxi, Fujian, and Jiangxi Provinces also Suspend Shipments of Finished Leather to Guangdong

Guangzhou Dispatch: Recently, excessive tax levies on cattle hides in Guangdong have led to strikes by leather manufacturers and cattle slaughterhouses. The root cause of this issue lies with the new company contracted to collect taxes on cattle hides, which has imposed exorbitant levies, provoking widespread opposition from the leather industry. Previously, Guangzhou only taxed raw hides, but the new tax collector has extended levies to finished leather. Moreover, hides entering the market from neighboring provinces are also subject to taxation. Leather merchants, burdened by these multiple layers of taxation, have repeatedly petitioned the Finance Department, requesting an improvement to the tax system to alleviate their burden. According to the leather merchants, in May of this year, a new tax collector, Mr. Chen, using the name of Guangheng Company, contracted with the Finance Department to collect taxes on slaughtered cattle hides and raw cattle hide exports. He altered the old tax regulations, leaving the tax on each slaughtered head of cattle unchanged. However, the tax on each hide was previously one dollar for a large hide and fifty cents for a small hide, but the new regulations make no distinction between sizes and uniformly levy 2.4 silver dollars per hide. The most unbearable aspect is that no distinction is made between sizes, and some small hides are worth only two or three dollars, or even just over one dollar, but the tax levied often exceeds the value. Furthermore, each slaughtered head of cattle is worth, on average, over one hundred dollars, with a tax of only two dollars, while each hide, regardless of size, is worth several dollars but is taxed 2.4 dollars. This is a reversal of priorities. Even worse, raw hides that have been taxed are taxed again after being processed into finished leather. The tax collector exploits the word "cattle hide" in the new regulations, disregarding whether the hide is raw or finished and levying taxes accordingly. Recently, inspectors have been dispatched, and if a peddler is found buying a half-dollar piece of finished leather, they are accused of evading taxes, the goods are confiscated, and the person is detained and fined, driving the leather industry to the brink of ruin. To survive, the leather industry feels compelled to argue their case. On the afternoon of the 15th, leather merchants gathered with their colleagues and held a joint meeting in a restaurant, with each business sending a representative. On that day, they decided to send representatives to various authorities to petition for redress. If the government continues to be misled by merchants seeking to harm others and disregards the plight of the merchants, they will have no choice but to strike collectively. The raw hide trade and the cattle slaughtering industry had already ceased operations and slaughtering on the 14th and 15th. On the 14th, the leather tanning industry in Bajiaoliao sent a letter to the cattle pen, halting purchases of raw hides and effectively ceasing tanning operations. Upon receiving the letter, the cattle pen operators, noting the complete halt of hide sales, also ceased slaughtering on the 15th, following the example of the leather tanners. Because beef is a staple food for city residents, the sudden absence of beef for sale on the 15th caused great inconvenience. Some vendors selling beef brought in from the suburbs charged over eighty cents per catty. Consequently, all beef-related food items in restaurants and teahouses were also discontinued. In addition, the leather brokerages in Foshan and Guangzhou had already gone on strike the day before, and the unrest is intensifying. Due to Guangdong's tax on finished leather from neighboring provinces, leather dealers from Guangxi, Fujian, and Jiangxi have also collectively ceased shipping finished leather to Guangdong in recent days. (August 16th)

The Turmoil of Increased Cigarette Taxes in Hebei Province 64

British and American Tobacco Factories Suspend Operations to Protest Taxes

Over Three Thousand Male and Female Workers Lose Jobs

Tianjin Dispatch: The original cigarette tax rate was 12% of the value, and even with the added special levy on smokers, it was no more than 15%. Two years ago, the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing implemented a unified cigarette tax, changing the rate to 32.5% of the value. At that time, a contract was signed with British, American, and Great American companies, stipulating that the tax rate could not be changed for two years. This agreement was set to expire on November 30th of this year. The Hebei Province Unified Cigarette Tax Bureau had been complying with this agreement. However, since the start of military operations this year, the tax revenue has not been reported to the central government but has been remitted to Taiyuan, amounting to approximately 500,000 to 700,000 dollars per month. In June, a Mr. Wang, the northern manager of a major Chinese tobacco company, petitioned the military authorities to increase the unified cigarette tax due to the stagnation in sales of over a thousand boxes of cigarettes, valued at around 300,000 dollars, stored in Tianjin. His intention was that an increase in taxes would hurt the sales of British and American cigarettes, allowing Chinese cigarettes to sell more freely. At that time, the northern military expenses were becoming exhausted, and the authorities naturally agreed to increase the tax. They dispatched Mr. Wang to negotiate with the British and American companies, but the companies stated that they would naturally support an increase in taxes to help the military and were willing to purchase two million dollars worth of unified tax stamps in advance to demonstrate their sincerity. Mr. Wang believed this to be true and reported this to the headquarters in Taiyuan. Yan Xishan immediately ordered an increase in the tax, changing the rate from 32.5% to 50% of the value. Initially, the Chinese tobacco merchants opposed this, but after repeated unsuccessful appeals, they reluctantly accepted the increase. The new tax rate was implemented on July 21st, and Great American had also accepted the increase. However, British American expressed their dissent, stating that the contract for 32.5% of the value would not expire until November 30th and that the tax could not be increased at this time. Despite repeated attempts by the Unified Tax Bureau to communicate, no progress was made. Although British American had not accepted the tax increase, retail cigarette shops were already increasing their prices by 30%. British American has a factory in Dawangzhuang, Tianjin, employing over three thousand male and female workers. Its products are sold in Hebei, Jehol, Chahar, Suiyuan, Henan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Shanxi, and Xinjiang provinces, with annual sales reaching over thirty million dollars. Since the implementation of the tax increase, the company has stopped shipping goods and has wired its Shanghai headquarters to stop shipments to Tianjin. The Tianjin factory has been continuing to operate, working only five days a week, because it has too much stored tobacco and is concerned about mold in the rainy season. On the 9th of this month, the Shanghai headquarters sent manager Hegede to Tianjin to investigate. Seeing that the warehouses were full of cigarette boxes and could not accommodate more, the company decided to suspend operations from the 11th onward, as further production would require renting additional warehouses. However, the factory needed to complete some tasks before suspending operations, so the cutting, steaming, sorting, and boxing departments were only shut down on the 13th. On the same day, half a month's wages were paid to the workers, and deposits for male workers were scheduled to be returned on the 18th, and for female workers on the 19th. Simultaneously, the Shanghai headquarters and the Tianjin municipal government were notified of the suspension. Mayor Cui immediately warned the Tianjin company's manager, Pille, and comprador, Zhang Xiaohang: (1) If the company suspends operations due to business stagnation, it should first submit a request to the local authorities. If it seeks a reduction in taxes, it should also first make a request. Only after permission is denied can the suspension be considered complete. During this period of military martial law, with the Communist Party poised to act, a sudden suspension of operations, disregarding the livelihoods of over three thousand male and female workers, could lead to unrest and affect social order, for which your company will be held responsible. The Public Security Bureau will have corresponding measures to deal with the situation as its duty dictates. (2) Most of British American's customers are Chinese. If the company suspends operations solely to protest the tax increase, the Chinese people may seize this opportunity to launch a boycott of British American cigarettes, causing even greater losses for your company. (3) Tobacco is a consumable good, and imposing heavy taxes on it is equivalent to discouraging consumption, indirectly burdening the smokers, while the company suffers no loss. Why protest? However, Pille's attitude was firm and he did not accept Mayor Cui's advice. Today (the 14th) in the morning, the cigarette-making and boxing departments were also shut down, and the entire factory was shut down by 10 a.m. The factory gates were locked, and the company staff continued to work as usual, but shipments have stopped. The various British American cigarettes sold on the market are from the inventories of the distributors, who have contracts with the company that prohibit them from selling other companies' tobacco. The four hundred or so British American cigarette distributors in the city have inventories that can only sustain business for twenty days at most. After that, they will have no cigarettes to sell and will have to close down. Gao Huai, the director of the Unified Cigarette Tax Bureau, stated that this tax increase, nominally 50% of the value, is actually only an increase of 17.5%. Other Chinese and foreign tobacco companies have complied with the tax regulations and paid the taxes. British American is the only one dissenting and protesting the tax by suspending operations, which is akin to extortion. The bureau is acting under orders and has no prejudice in the matter. Today, a telegram has been sent to Taiyuan to await instructions. Before receiving instructions from Taiyuan, goods from that company that have not paid the increased tax will continue to be impounded. According to a survey by the cigarette merchants' association, cigarette sales in the city have decreased by 568,000 dollars in the twenty days since the implementation of the tax increase on July 21st, compared to the average for June and July. The Unified Tax Bureau has lost 284,000 dollars in revenue. At 9 a.m. today, Zhu Ziqi, a publicly elected representative, took these charts and a petition to Zhao Pilian in Beiping, requesting assistance. However, Mr. Pille intends not to resume operations until the old tax rate is restored, even if it results in significant losses. At 4 p.m. today, he visited Mayor Cui to report that all operations have been suspended and that the factory staff have closed the books. If there is no solution, the staff will be dismissed. Mayor Cui replied that the municipal government has no authority to interfere with tax payment, but the suspension of operations affects the city's security and the workers' livelihoods, which cannot be ignored. Furthermore, the current tax increase, nominally 50%, is actually only an increase of 17.5%, directly affecting the company and indirectly affecting the smokers. The losses from the suspension are greater than the tax payment. Please reconsider, and so on.

Page 10

Important News Two 65

Pille retreated without making any significant concessions. Mayor Cui immediately instructed the secretariat to draft another warning letter to the company, urging the company to resume operations. It is also said that Cui will send someone to mediate tomorrow, which may lead to a compromise solution. (August 14th)

Disputes over the Four Cotton and Linen Factories in Hubei Province 66

Private Shares Unpaid After Joint Government-Private Operation

Manager of Fuyuan Company Arrested Hankou Dispatch: Near Yellow Crane Tower in Wuchang, there are four cotton, linen, cloth, and silk factories established by the government, employing over six thousand three hundred workers. The establishment of the four factories can be traced back to the late Qing Dynasty, when Zhang Zhidong governed the Two Lakes region. Recognizing the encroachment of foreign goods and the hardships of the people, he established the four factories to promote industry, resist foreign goods, and maintain the livelihoods of the common people. After the establishment of the Republic of China, the factories were taken over by the Hubei provincial government. Later, due to losses, they were reorganized as private enterprises, with the provincial government only collecting rent and profit dividends, and renamed Fuyuan Company. In the past two years, Fuyuan Company has suffered further losses, with the machinery dilapidated and not repaired, resulting in lower production and greater losses. In February of this year, the company announced its closure, leaving all six thousand three hundred workers unemployed. In May, the Hubei provincial government, concerned that the large number of unemployed workers would affect society and that allowing such a large enterprise to remain closed would be a loss of resources, ordered Huang Meisheng, the general manager of Fuyuan Company, to resume operations as soon as possible. Huang, citing his inability to resume operations, petitioned the authorities for a joint government-private operation. The provincial government approved the request and set the capital at one million dollars, with the Hubei provincial government and Fuyuan Company each contributing half. A contract was signed, and Zhou Huangchu was appointed by the Finance Department as the manager of the four factories. The name was changed to Gongyi Company. The Finance Department issued two hundred thousand dollars in government shares to prepare for the resumption of operations and to pay off the five thousand three hundred fifty-four dollars in back wages owed by Fuyuan Company to the workers. The factories were scheduled to officially reopen on August 20th. The workers were overjoyed upon hearing the news, hoping for a swift return to work. Unexpectedly, the Fuyuan Company's commitment of five hundred thousand dollars in private shares has not yet been paid, and the outstanding rent of over four hundred thirty thousand dollars for the factories has not been settled, causing preparations to stall and delaying the reopening. The newly appointed manager, Zhou Huangchu, reported the reason for the failure to open the factories to He Yingqin, the head of the Wuhan headquarters. Yesterday, the headquarters sent a telegram ordering Huang Meisheng, the general manager of Fuyuan Company, to be placed under the custody of the Wuchang Public Security Bureau. After other related parties are apprehended, their dues will be pursued and they will be punished according to law. Therefore, these thousands of workers are now quietly waiting for the authorities to resolve their predicament. (August 20th)

Floods and Banditry in Henan Province 67

Mengjin Flood and Banditry Relief Request Telegram To Xu Jun, Chairman of the Nanjing Relief Commission; Shanghai, Beiping, and Tianjin Charity Organizations: According to Zhang Shushen, the magistrate of Mengjin County, the county is the poorest in Henan Province, and the people are suffering from successive disasters. Currently, the military expenditures are enormous, and they are still trying to supply them in the hopes of an early resolution and temporary relief. However, on July 9th, the river north of the county broke its banks, flooding over a hundred square li in the northeast, turning it into a swamp. Towns such as Youfang Street, North Pass, East Pass, Xiaoji, and Shuanghuai Garden were all swept away by the flood, destroying fields, homes, people, and livestock. After requesting and obtaining permission to investigate and raise funds for relief, on the 14th, bandits suddenly emerged from the territory of Luoyang and Yanshi, besieging the county seat on the west, south, and north sides for three days and nights. Nearby villages were burned and looted. The city was in danger of falling, but fortunately, the Gan Army's Ma Brigade arrived, and the bandits fled south. On the 16th, Hengshui Town in the west of the city was attacked by bandits from Xin'an, who burned and killed indiscriminately. The town's militia chased them to Laodawo in Xin'an. On the evening of the 17th, two groups of bandits came to areas such as Zhencun and Wutou in Xin'an, besieging our militia, who are currently engaged in a fierce battle awaiting reinforcements. Since June 9th, the towns of Chen'ao, Matun, and Wangzhuang in the west of the county have suffered from banditry, resulting in nearly ten thousand deaths and injuries and thousands of kidnapped hostages. All the civilian property in the county has either been washed away or reduced to ashes. Corpses are scattered everywhere, and cries of grief fill the night. We earnestly request you to forward this information and provide relief to alleviate the suffering of the people. Lishen, Chairman of the Henan Relief Association, kowtows.

Yiyang Banditry Relief Request Telegram To Shanghai and Beiping Charity Organizations: According to Cao Yaozu, the magistrate of Yiyang County, the east and west villages of Hancheng Town in the county were simultaneously attacked and captured by bandits. Bandit leader Sun Yaoguang and over two thousand others occupied the town for more than a month, killing over five hundred people, burning hundreds of houses, and looting all the property and food. The burning and killing in the affiliated villages of Qinwang Village and six other villages was even more horrific. There are few houses left in the other nearby villages. Before leaving, they kidnapped over eight hundred hostages, leaving behind only scorched earth and starving survivors. We urgently request you to provide relief to alleviate the suffering of the people. Lishen, Chairman of the Henan Relief Association, kowtows.

The Finance Department, based on a petition from various merchants in Yunhe County, alleges that Shen Rentian, general manager of the Ou Salt Office tax collection and transportation office, and Cheng Taihe, manager of the Yunhe branch, are monopolizing, hoarding, and raising prices, requesting that the concession for both the Wenzhou and Chuzhou offices be canceled to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. Local Communications

Songjiang 69

False Alarm Reported in Jingjia Weir Last night (20th) around 11 p.m., three people resembling soldiers were spotted lurking on the roof of the Wang family's house near the Yanshengtang west of Malu Bridge. The owner, Mr. Wang, was alarmed and immediately reported it to the Military and Police Inspection Office, which dispatched a team to investigate. As a result, one person was apprehended on the roof, who claimed that he and two others were there due to financial difficulties. The other two were subsequently apprehended and are temporarily detained at the Inspection Office, before being transferred to the 1st Regiment of the Anti-Smuggling Department for further investigation.

Plane Gets Lost and Lands Around 6 p.m. today, the sound of grinding could be heard in the sky, and then a gray airplane was seen circling the city four or five times, sometimes high, sometimes low, drawing crowds of onlookers. Unexpectedly, it suddenly crashed into a small river next to the old Discipline Department's former parade ground. The four pilots were unharmed, and the plane was undamaged. It is said that it was traveling from Shanghai to Hangzhou but got lost and mistook this place for Hangzhou, hence the descent.

Suspect Female Temporarily Released on Bail On the 19th, a woman named Wang Bihua returned from Shanghai to Hangzhou, passing through Songjiang, where she was stopped by military police for carrying contraband. She was forced to get off the bus, and Wang, under the pretext of needing to urinate, fled into the city and went to the county government for help. The county magistrate and the Public Security Bureau investigated and found that the woman, Wang, did not admit to carrying contraband. She has been temporarily released on bail by the Public Security Bureau.

Suzhou 70

Inspection Office Investigates Those Impersonating Soldiers The military and police joint inspection office has recently discovered that a group of people wearing incomplete military uniforms are impersonating soldiers or falsely recruiting laborers, deceiving the people, and attempting to defraud them of their money. This is extremely illegal. Yesterday, it specially sent letters to the water and land police and the Chamber of Commerce to investigate and deal with this matter. Anyone wearing incomplete military uniforms without insignia will also be arrested.

Newly Built Jinmen Archway Collapses, Injuring People The newly opened Jinmen, on the right side of Xin Qimen, was contracted to Shen Zaixing's Construction Factory. The Construction Bureau ordered it to be completed by the 20th of this month, but Shen requested a postponement, which was approved for ten days, with completion required by the end of the month. Yesterday (21st) around 10 a.m., while the scaffolding was being removed from the right-side archway-style rampart, it suddenly collapsed two-thirds of the way due to excessive weight, breaking the ankle and head in two places of a worker named Dai A'yu. Wu A'song was also seriously injured. Two apprentices, Tao Sheng and Xiao Nan, also suffered minor injuries. The injured were immediately taken to Gengsheng Hospital for treatment. Dai and Wu are feared to be in danger of death. The Construction Bureau will also punish the contractor, Shen Zaixing, for cutting corners and causing this disaster.

Property Management Office Reorganized into Relief Institute The Wuxian County Public Property Management Office has been ordered to close and reorganize into a relief institute. County Magistrate Huang has specially appointed former Wuxian County Education Bureau Director Wang Guoxiang as the director and Chen Xilian as the deputy director.

Public Security Bureau Director Accused In the case against Zou Xiaogong, the director of the Wuxian County Public Security Bureau, County Magistrate Huang had previously been instructed by the Civil Affairs Department to investigate and respond. After County Magistrate Huang truthfully reported the matter, yesterday he received instructions to order the director to strengthen his efforts in arresting bandits and suppressing opium and gambling, and not to neglect his duties again.

Zhang Taijie's Appeal Case The former director of the Sichuan-Han Highway Office, Zhang Taijie, established the Sichuan-Han Highway Shanghai Office at No. 51 Wuxing Lane, Beiler Road, in the French Concession of Shanghai. Last year, he was accused by Sichuanese individuals Zeng Xianzhi, Lei Jianhou, and Liu Yajue at the Shanghai District Court of embezzling highway funds and illegally selling a plot of land in Hankou for 2,500 dollars. After being summoned by the District Court in January of this year and arrested due to the importance of the case, he was repeatedly tried. The case was complex, involving the lawyer Dong Yu embezzling 20,000 taels of public funds and pocketing 13,000 taels. The verdict was announced on July 1st of this year, finding Zhang Taijie guilty of embezzlement and sentencing him to three years in prison. Zhang, dissatisfied with the verdict, hired lawyer Yang Yinhang and appealed to the High Court. The High Court was scheduled to open the trial yesterday morning (21st), with Lin Dawen, the presiding judge of the First Criminal Tribunal, presiding. Summonses were issued to nine respondents: Zeng Xianzhi, Lei Jianhou, Liu Yajue, Chen Shujia, lawyer Dong Yu, lawyer Li Shirui, Cheng Zhongfan, Ao Enzhan, and Wu Jingming. Only Zeng Xianzhi, lawyer Dong Yu, and Ao Enzhan reported. The appellant, Zhang Taijie, requested a postponement of the trial on the grounds that his defense lawyer, Yang Yinhang, had not yet reviewed the case files. Presiding Judge Lin granted the request and instead opened an inquiry.

Wuxi 71

Reactions to Education Budget Cuts Former County Magistrate Sun Zuji, because of the severe financial difficulties in the region, has carried years of cumulative losses, and has been unable to remedy the situation, and has been forced to implement austerity policies. At the previous county administration meeting, he deliberated and decided to cut more than 40,000 yuan from the education budget for the nineteenth year. The County Education Bureau and the principals of the county's schools were of the opinion that the education funding in Wuxi was already extremely tight, and if it were cut further, it would be difficult to maintain. They repeatedly argued with the county government, but ultimately, without additional funds, there was no solution. The principals of the county's schools, with the start of the semester approaching, have not yet determined the education funding. Although they had repeatedly urged the director of the County Education Bureau to find a solution, they have not received a reply, which they take as a lack of sincerity. Yesterday, they held a general meeting at the County Education Association and resolved to: (1) send representatives to urge them again; (2) if there is still no satisfactory response after the urging, indicating that the bureau has no sincerity in maintaining the situation, in order to avoid future difficulties, issue a joint notice from the county's schools to unanimously postpone the start of the semester, awaiting a solution, and also petition higher authorities for instructions and inform the local elders to uphold justice. At the same time, the educational branch associations in various cities and villages held a meeting at the County Education Association and resolved that: ad valorem taxes should be used entirely for salary increases, bonuses, and subsidies for educational branch associations, and that old salary increases should at least be restored to the original plan, and a special committee should be organized to strongly argue with the county government and the Education Bureau. If the arguments are ineffective, all schools will go on strike simultaneously. The number of people on the special committee will be seven; (3) after the education funds are secured, the director of the Education Bureau should be responsible for guaranteeing that they are not used or reduced by anyone.

First District Office Takes Over the Park The City Park in Xiyi was previously managed by Zhou Jimei, a local, and the park's operations were becoming increasingly corrupt, and the citizens were all dissatisfied. Recently, the first regular meeting of the City Property Management Committee decided to transfer the City Park to the First District Office for management. The county government has also issued a public letter transferring the matter to Qian, the head of the district, for investigation and handling. After receiving the order, Qian immediately commissioned a staff member, Chen Hanxiang, to take the public letter to take over the park on the morning of yesterday (21st). It is also said that a director and a manager will be appointed in accordance with the provisional park management regulations, specializing in management, and that several fair-minded local individuals will be hired to form a park design committee to plan everything.

Bandits in Yinshazhou Strangle Old Woman Wang Chen, a native of Anhui, lived in Yinshazhou, the third district of Wuyi. She was 72 years old and had some savings. County Magistrate Li Secretly Interrogates Chen Weiwu for the Second Time A resident of Rizhao Township in the tenth district captured a Communist Party member named Chen Weiwu, alias Wang Guozhen, in Zhulin'an. Because Chen confessed that he knew Xu Yan and Wang Ping, on the 19th, the Public Security Bureau ordered the Detective Team to summon Xu Yan to the case. County Magistrate Li presented Chen Weiwu for confrontation. According to Xu Yan, he had always been loyal and was surprised to be summoned for no reason. As for Wang Ping, he is now in Suzhou and has been sentenced for counter-revolutionary crimes. The year before, when he was serving as a trainer for the city's defense regiment, he arrested and prosecuted him. Chen said that Xu is currently not a Communist Party member. Three years ago, because he joined the Kuomintang, I expelled him from the party. After being expelled, he had no work. County Magistrate Li, seeing that Xu had no connection, ordered him to be released on bail. He asked Chen whether there were any Communist Party organizations in the urban area. Chen said that there were a total of eighteen district branches in the county, two in the urban area, ten in Qingchang, three in the southeastern township, and three in Xiagang. After the interrogation, Chen was detained.

Nantong 75

Conference on Joint Defense and Suppression in Five Counties of Tongtai: The Provincial Security Office of the Civil Affairs Department, considering the rampant banditry in the five counties of Tongtai in Jiangbei, ordered Li Changjiang, head of the Third Security Regiment, to convene the county magistrates of the five counties in Tongcheng on the 20th to hold a conference on joint defense and suppression. The county magistrates attending were Zhang Dong of Nantong, Zhang Yi of Taixian, Qian Zuoyi of Rugao, Wang Jiwu of Jingjiang, and Ma Rensheng of Taixing. Provincial security regiment officers Xie Jicang, Xia Zhen, and Yu Shimei were also present. Regiment Leader Li chaired the meeting, which lasted from 2 p.m. to 8 p.m. A plan for joint defense and suppression of communist bandits in the five counties was formulated. Small groups of local bandits are to be eliminated by the counties themselves, and after the suppression, the counties must take over the work of clearing the countryside and preventing bandits. The matters of defense and suppression will be reported to the Provincial Department and Office by Regiment Leader Li for approval and implementation.

Fundraising for Local Public Bonds by the Loan and Property Office: The local finances of Tongyi have recently suffered a shortfall of over 90,000 yuan, putting it in a desperate situation. Zhenjiang 76

Public Security Bureau Conducts Large-Scale Inspection: Chen Fu, Director of the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, believes that Zhenjiang, as the provincial capital, is a place where people from all directions gather, and it is easy for petty thieves to hide. In order to fundamentally eliminate them, a large-scale inspection must be carried out so that criminals have nowhere to hide, and hidden worries can be eliminated. Therefore, he instructed the various branch bureaus to carry out the large-scale inspection yesterday morning. All shantytowns, hotels, and public places within the territory were searched extensively, but no discoveries of note were made.

Merchants Oppose Telephone Rate Increase: The Zhenjiang Telephone Bureau, upon receiving instructions from the Ministry of Communications, increased the rental fee for each user by one yuan (silver dollar), for a total of six yuan, due to the soaring price of gold and the fact that telephone materials are all purchased from foreign countries, resulting in a doubling of costs. This was notified to all users yesterday, and will be implemented uniformly from September 1st. However, various merchants and shops believe that Zhenjiang's telephones are already unreliable, and the price increase at a time of commercial recession is causing even greater dissatisfaction. Therefore, they jointly submitted a petition to the Chamber of Commerce yesterday, requesting that it be forwarded to the Ministry, requesting that the order for the price increase be rescinded in order to maintain the status quo.

Yangzhou 77

Continued Report on Bandits Kidnapping Children and Injuring People: In Aozi Street outside the Dongguan of this city, the Chen and Zhang families had two children, a boy and a girl, kidnapped by bandits the night before, and a son of the Dong family and a Cao were shot and injured. It is now learned that after the case occurred, the victim Chen Jintao reported the case to various government offices. It is reported that the county government immediately ordered the dispatch of a detective team to conduct a strict search inside and outside the city yesterday (the 19th). It was also reported that a small boat was found in the Dongjiagou in the Shahe Dam outside Dongguan, which was considered suspicious. Upon interrogation, it was learned that the boat was transporting a patient from the countryside to the city for medical treatment. After being vouched for by someone, there were no other suspicions. In addition, someone surnamed, who usually made a living selling pens in Aozi Street, saw a kidnapped Chen girl outside the South Gate yesterday and asked her why she was here. The girl replied that she had been abducted by kidnappers. The pen seller immediately reported this to the victim's family, and a detective team has now been dispatched for a secret investigation. As for Dong's child's ear, because it was severely injured, he could not eat, and even if he was fed chicken broth and boiled water, it would enter his mouth and then come out of his nose. According to the doctor, his condition is very dangerous. If he can survive for five days, there is still hope for recovery.

Huzhou 78

Village Chiefs of Three Subordinate Areas Kidnapped and Rescued: Shen Meijiang, the village chief of Sanyang Village in Houshengbu, Guoxi Xun, southwest of this city, had some assets and had long been coveted by bandits. In order to avoid banditry, Shen moved to the city in the autumn of the 16th year of the Republic. On the first day of this month, while traveling by boat to his hometown, only three miles from the port, he saw eight bandits speaking with a Henan accent and holding handguns on the shore, ordering the boat to stop. The bandits boarded the boat and kidnapped Shen Meijiang and his fellow passenger Pan Deshun. Later, Shen's family tried to rescue him, but failed due to various reasons. Unexpectedly, on the 16th, the security team stationed in Meixi sent someone to Huzhou to tell Shen's family that a hostage named Shen Meijiang had been captured by the villagers of Heping Liqi Village, and asked his family to go and claim him. Shen's younger brother, Meichun, went to the company headquarters of the Meixi security team upon hearing the news and confirmed that it was true. He immediately identified him, and the company sent ten soldiers to escort him home on a steamer on the 19th. Shen Meijiang has been in the bandits' den for nearly two weeks. Now, the details of what happened are described as follows: According to Shen, after he and Pan Deshun were kidnapped, they were moved five or six times, all in the Henan straw huts in the mountains of Heping. Each time, their eyes were tightly blindfolded with cloth, and they were carried by the bandits. Usually, three bandits guarded the hostages. On the morning of the 14th, because Pan Deshun's family had already paid the ransom, Pan was accompanied by a bandit to Heping Town to take a boat back to Huzhou. Shen himself was carried by two bandits to a straw hut near Liqi Village, about 14 li from Heping. One bandit went out on business, and the other guarded outside the hut. This was glimpsed by the villagers of the village, and more than 30 members of the village's self-defense corps, each carrying an earthen gun, shot and killed the guarding bandit. Shen immediately explained the situation of his kidnapping to the members of the corps, and they sent him to the Heping Town Defense Corps. The next day, he was transferred to the company headquarters of the Meixi security team. Now, the company has sent soldiers to escort him back to Huzhou.

Yan was injured and ran to the Public Security Bureau, and then transferred to the court for examination. Xiao-Chang Road to Open to Traffic This Year: The earthwork for the Xiao-Chang Road from Xiaoshan to Jianshan section has been completed early. Jiashan 81

A slow train No. 7 was approaching and sounded a warning when it saw the old woman wandering on the road. However, the old woman was old and deaf and could not avoid it in time, and was crushed to death by the train. Her blood and flesh flew everywhere, and her body was almost in pieces, which was heartbreaking to see. Her family has been notified to collect the body.

Small Boat Racing Causes Disaster: The shuttle boats between Anting Station on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and Taicang-Anting in the county are operated by Taixing Company, followed by Taian Company. All the boats are extremely crowded with passengers. Since the 10th of this month, Taian has been competing for business by reducing fares and increasing speeds, in order to be the first to arrive at the port. On the afternoon of the 17th, the company's Xieli, carrying passengers from An Station to Tai, when approaching the Xiabutu Wharf outside the West Gate, the driver, Lao Daou, was careless, and the bow of the boat collided violently with the bridge base of Xixin Bridge, causing a huge hole and sinking on the spot. Fortunately, the water was shallow and narrow, and the passengers were unharmed, but the hull has not been salvaged to this day, which is a hindrance to waterway traffic.

Important Educational News

Problem of Adding Classrooms to Elementary Schools 85

One Million Classrooms Need to be Added Nationwide

An Average of More Than 500 Classrooms Need to be Added Per County

The outline of the plan to implement compulsory education has been approved by the Second National Education Conference. However, the addition of classrooms in elementary schools is a major problem. According to a senior official of the Ministry of Education, it is estimated that it will cost at least 200 yuan to renovate an old-fashioned house into a classroom, and about 300 yuan for various equipment needed in each classroom, for a total start-up cost of 500 yuan to open a class. One million classrooms need to be added nationwide. There are 1,915 counties in the country, and an average of more than 500 classrooms need to be added per county. Given the financial difficulties in various localities, it is only possible to use the ancestral temples of people across the country to open elementary schools, and to use academic palaces, academies, and public places. This has already been implemented in most places. In addition, it is also necessary to use all temples and monasteries, and to encourage private donations of houses or funds to build schools. The government should also plan and build a type of school building that is extremely economical and durable, and publicly set a simple and practical standard for equipment for various localities to adopt. Part of the subsidies allocated by the central government and the national treasury should be used as funds for building school buildings.

Religious Electives May Be Established in Schools Above High School 86

Completely Abolished in Schools Below High School

Jinling Women's University Will Be Closed for Not Being Registered

The Ministry of Education has already issued a notice to all schools to comply with the cancellation of religious courses in church schools. Now, regulations have been stipulated that schools above high school may establish one elective course, which students may freely choose to join, but cannot be forced to. All schools below high school will be completely abolished and not allowed to exist. The schools had previously jointly petitioned for restoration, but this has been rejected.

According to a secretary of the Ministry, Jinling Women's University was ordered by the Ministry to go through the procedures for registration. To date, it has not been fulfilled, which is in violation of the law. After the summer vacation, if the school still does not comply with the regulations and register, the Ministry will have the power to close the school.

Reduction of Public Expenses for Liaoning Students Studying in Japan 90

Tuition Fees Changed to Be Issued According to National Currency

Significant Impact of Gold Expensive and Silver Cheap

Shenyang Communication: Before the 14th year of the Republic, the Provincial Education Department stipulated that the monthly tuition fee for each public-funded student studying in Japan was 15 Japanese yen. At that time, the currency value was similar to the national currency. In the 17th year, the students studying in Japan, due to the high cost and high cost of living, jointly requested the Ningxia Provincial Education Department to increase the fees, originally requesting that each person be increased to 60 yuan (Japanese yen) per month. The late Director Wang Yugui did not approve it because the tuition fees had increased several times, requiring huge funds and affecting the budget. Later, the students obtained the approval of Commander Zhang Xueliang to change each person to 60 Japanese yen per month and to change the tuition fee to an incentive bonus, which was very effective. At that time, the value of the Japanese yen had risen to about 1.2 yuan in national currency. Since the gold rush began this year, the Japanese yen has suddenly risen to about 2 yuan in national currency per day. The incentive bonus for each student is 60 Japanese yen. Calculated according to the 92 public-funded students studying in Japan in the province, the annual cost is 66,240 Japanese yen, equivalent to 132,480 yuan in national currency (calculated at 2 yuan in national currency per 1 Japanese yen). Compared with the 17th year, the budget must be exceeded by more than 50,000 yuan. The difference is huge, and the impact is quite large. The shortage of school funds has become difficult to cope with. If the Japanese yen continues to rise, the loss will be even greater. The Education Department considered the situation and planned to cancel the original fixed Japanese yen issuance and switch to issuing national currency. However, in order to take into account both the living expenses of studying abroad, the national currency issued was increased by 20 yuan from the original Japanese yen, to 80 yuan, and the annual amount per person was 960 yuan, so that the study abroad expenses would not cause panic due to depletion. After submitting it to the provincial government for review and approval, it can be implemented next semester. However, among the general students studying in Japan, except for a part of those who are wealthy, there will not be too much difficulty. For the rest, such as those who rely on tuition fees for admission and all expenses, I am afraid that there will be no shortage of dropouts.

News from the Experimental Area for Universal Education of the Suzhou Education Department 92

Concord University Alumni Welcome the President 102

President Lin Reports on the University's Recent Developments

Discussion of the 15th Anniversary Celebration

Fujian Concord University has been in operation for fifteen years and has a well-organized internal structure divided into four colleges: Arts, Sciences, Education, and Pre-Medical. It can be considered one of the best universities in the country. It now has hundreds of graduates, and a considerable number of them are in Shanghai. The Shanghai alumni of the university held a discussion about the university's 15th anniversary celebration and also hosted a banquet for the university's president, Professor Lin Jingrun, and Zeng Kexi. They gathered at the Da Zhonghua Restaurant on Sichuan Road last night at 7:00 PM. Alumni attended enthusiastically, including Huang Jiahuai, Xu Shaoshan, Wei Xiben, Chen Guanxiang, Huang Jiali, Lin Chengshui, and Li Zhi'an, among others, totaling more than thirty people. First, President Lin reported on the university's recent developments, which can be divided into several aspects: (1) Regarding buildings, a new Arts and Sciences building worth over 200,000 yuan has recently been completed. It has three floors. The first floor houses the offices of the president, academic dean, college deans, and department heads, as well as a large auditorium. The second floor houses the classrooms of each department. The third floor houses the library. The interior equipment and decorations are not only highly scientific but also artistically rich. In addition, there is a student dormitory that can accommodate one hundred students and a faculty residence building. (2) Regarding registration matters, the results of several contacts with the Ministry of Education have been very satisfactory. It is expected that the official announcement will be made by the end of this month. (3) Regarding university affairs, there were one hundred and fifty students last year, and more than ten new faculty and staff members were hired, all of whom are renowned scholars from home and abroad. It has also been decided to admit female students starting next semester, and it is expected that the number of students will break all previous records. (4) Regarding finances, the university received a large donation from an American philanthropist last year, so there are ample funds for recurring expenses. (5) The university has been established for fifteen years, and it has been decided to hold a grand commemorative meeting next semester. All alumni are invited to attend to rekindle old memories. After President Lin's report, the entire group discussed the Shanghai alumni's commemorative activities for the 15th anniversary and elected Huang Jiahuai, Xu Shaoshan, Wei Xiben, and Chen Guanxiang as preparation committee members to hold a general meeting on a selected date. It was also decided to tentatively designate Wei Xiben's office at the All Saints Church on Lafayette Road in the French Concession as the Shanghai Alumni Association office. All alumni of the university in Shanghai who have not yet joined are requested to report their detailed addresses to Mr. Wei for communication purposes. The meal ended at 10:30 PM, and everyone departed happily.
