Free Talk

Dismissing with a Laugh 110

— Hai Ke

Celebrity (bursting into the editor's office of a certain newspaper, fuming) — This is outrageous! I'm alive and well. How dare you say I'm dead in today's obituary column? This absolutely must be corrected!

Editor — I don't think a correction is necessary. Tomorrow, we can just put you in the "Births" column. Give you a fresh start in life. Wouldn't that be wonderful?

A — I've done so many things in my life. Most of them went smoothly. Thinking back, the only thing that really disappointed me was something that happened when I was a child. I still haven't forgotten it.

B — What happened?

A — Once, I walked past a tent. Someone told me there was a circus inside, very exciting. I was thrilled and snuck in through the back. I really put my heart into it. But when I got up and looked around, there was no circus at all. Just an old man giving a sermon.

Old Man A — My child has been spoiled by his mother since he was little. We always indulged him. That's why he wants everything he sees now.

Old Man B — That's wonderful! Could you possibly bring him to my house for dinner one day? I'd like to introduce him to my eldest daughter.

Father — I think the kid's dimwitted. It definitely didn't come from my genes.

Mother — That's right. I think you're dimwitted, and it hasn't decreased at all. It shows that you didn't pass it on to him.

A Returnee from Fufeng Talks 111

— Xu Fan

The frequent natural disasters in the provinces of Shaanxi and Gansu have been astonishing. They've already been all over the newspapers. Although charities have been providing aid, the disaster areas are vast, and there are too many monks for too little gruel. It's hard to provide universal relief. My friend, Mr. Li, was commissioned by the Rescue Association to go there last winter to distribute aid. He spent half a year there. He's just returned. During our conversation the other day, I noted down the things he said that were most worth sharing.

Puyi Exchanges Fur for Virtue　Mr. Li and his party received a warm welcome from the locals as they passed through Hebei. At the time, the philanthropist Mr. Zhu Qinglan was advocating for disaster relief. He approached the deposed Emperor Puyi of the Qing Dynasty to ask for donations. Puyi, living in a small house in Tianjin, lacked the ability to turn lead into gold. He reluctantly offered five hundred light fur coats and many precious treasures to help with the relief efforts. However, the fox furs were splendid but not appropriate for the occasion. They were eventually sold through a lottery system. There was a frenzy of buying, and in the end, it was exchanged for 150,000 foreign Buddhas. The people of Tianjin and Beijing considered it a beautiful story. Everyone joked that even though the deposed emperor was poor, he still had three loads of copper. The saying fit well and he still deserved the title of a poor old boss. I read in the newspaper before that Puyi had a diamond and was looking to sell it. Now I believe it even more.

Yansheng Presents Sacrificial Vessels to Guests　The disasters were most severe in the counties of Fufeng and Wugong in Shaanxi Province. Mr. Li and his party carried money and food and divided into two teams upon arrival: one for burying the dead and one for distributing relief. They distributed aid to each household based on the number of people. They provided seeds to help with cultivation and stopped only after the autumn harvest of the following year. Hundreds of miles were filled with wailing, and the lives of those who were sustained for several months depended on them. The amount of money spent exceeded millions, but it was still not enough. It was truly a case of people relying on heaven for sustenance, but how long can people rely on that? The work of burying exposed corpses and digging mass graves was smelly and unbearable to witness. Compared to the prosperity of Shanghai, it was like being in another world. The group returned to Qufu and visited the mausoleum of Confucius. Yansheng Kong Decheng presented jade sacrificial vessels for inspection. The vessels gleamed like bronze and were truly unparalleled treasures, rarely seen in the world. It is said that even if military personnel visited, he wouldn't display everything. This shows his heart of treasure. Mr. Kong Decheng was only nine years old, but his attitude was solemn. He held a brush and wrote on the desk, reaching the small table. His calligraphy was elegant, his strokes strong, and his talent outstanding. He took a commemorative photo with the visitors before they left and also presented a couplet. Unfortunately, my memory is failing, and I can't recall the couplet.

Humble Opinions on Treating Dysentery 112

— Jie Lu

Dysentery is prevalent everywhere this summer. Cholera is extremely rare. (There are especially no cases found in Shanghai. This is likely due to the effectiveness of the promotion of vaccinations by the authorities.) The growth of bacteria is greatly related to the weather. Yesterday, I read "A Proven Prescription for Treating Dysentery" by the recluse Zhizhi in Free Talk. It uses peony soup, intending to promote bowel movements. The prescription is very good. However, the prescription uses two mace of rhubarb. Those who are physically weak and have had dysentery for a long time may not be able to withstand it. It would be better to reduce it to one mace. Western medicine treats dysentery. At the onset of the disease, one can fast for a day, not eating any food. On the afternoon of the second day, start taking a wine cup of castor oil, then half a grain of bismuth subnitrate, taking it once. Take it three times a day for two days. Diet should be very careful. Only use milk, thin porridge, and other easily digestible foods. Avoid raw, cold, and greasy foods. Also, injecting serum is very effective. Popularly, ash from hawthorn berries or a decoction of white cockscomb flowers can be taken with brown sugar for red dysentery or with yellow sugar for white dysentery. It is also very effective. As for preventative measures, one can get a dysentery vaccination or take "Vankexing Tablets" (orovaecin) internally. (Sold in major pharmacies and is also a preventative agent for cholera and typhoid fever.) Food should be clean. The abdomen should be kept warm at night. Have a bowel movement once a day. Bathe and massage frequently. Often rub the whole body with a dry cloth until it turns red. Or use the right hand to support the external genitals and massage the abdomen from top to bottom with the left hand. Then switch hands, using the left hand to support the external genitals and massage the abdomen from left to right, each massage done sixty times. This treats all abdominal diseases and is especially a great method for preventing dysentery. The bacteria of dysentery are often in the rectum. If it reaches the small intestine, it can be life-threatening. How can one not be careful?

Secrets in a Leather Bag 113

— Sheng Sheng

The autumn heat is like fire. One evening, my friend Mr. Chen Shangda came hurrying by, fanning himself with his right hand and carrying a leather bag in his left. He asked me to go to the Bund Park to cool off, saying that the horse-drawn carriage was waiting at the door and urging me to go immediately. Shangda is a bohemian and unconventional man. He is also curious by nature. Anything he hears or sees that is slightly strange, he writes down and puts in his leather bag. He never submits anything for publication. Taking advantage of his unpreparedness, I grabbed his leather bag first, joking, "Horse-drawn carriages are outdated now. Hurry and get a car so I can search for the secrets in this leather bag before we go." Shangda said, "One man's trash is another man's treasure. What's wrong with a horse-drawn carriage? There are indeed secrets in here. If you hadn't mentioned it, I would have told you anyway." He then took out a letter from the leather bag, addressed to Mr. Xie Mengren of Xin Chongqing Road, Shanghai, and signed by Huang Ji of Huzhou. It didn't specify the lane number. I exclaimed, "Did the post office misdeliver this?" He replied, "No, I found it on the road." The letter was very simple, just a few words: "My sister A'Hu, whom I dream of night after night, hasn't returned for a long time in this scorching heat. I know you're addicted to the taste of 'braised eel.'" There were a few words written on the back, in a delicate handwriting, apparently a reply from Huang to the original letter. It said, "Brother Ying, I haven't eaten any braised eel. Brother, you seem to have eaten 'vinegar-fried eel.' I'll be back soon. I won't betray you." This is secret number one. There was also a photo of a girl with her hair in a bun leaning on a concubine's couch, looking up at a handsome young man with clear eyes. Another photo showed a beautiful woman with a full face and a thick bun, holding a child and winking at the young man. I asked where they came from. Shangda said, "I write and paint and photograph. I painted them and photographed them myself." His words were very cunning and unbelievable. This is secret number two. There were many other things, but I didn't have time to examine them. He hurriedly dragged me out to the carriage. When we arrived at the park, there was a refreshing breeze and shimmering waves. Many couples were whispering or pretending to be angry or acting like Western couples, shoulder to shoulder, arm in arm. The sound of footsteps echoed as they walked back and forth. As we were about to leave, we saw a middle-aged woman walking hand in hand with a sad-looking young man. A little girl, just beginning to blossom, swayed her willow waist as she followed behind, calling to the young man, "Brother Ji!" She was chattering endlessly. Shangda said, "The world is a big leather bag. You don't examine the secrets in the big leather bag but instead search for secrets in my small leather bag. What a narrow view!" His words were also witty. So I recorded them.

A Kind Favor 114

— Jian Bai

It is a very common thing for friends to give gifts and reciprocate favors. For example, if a friend likes alcohol and you give them a "Xian Bo" wine, or if a friend likes calligraphy and painting and you give them a piece by a famous artist, the recipient will be overjoyed. They will feel that it is inappropriate to refuse and shameless to accept. Otherwise, it would be boring. I am very fond of stringed instruments and records of famous singers. The other day, my close friend, the famous erhu enthusiast Mr. Zhou Zhenfang, brought me two of his most prized records as a gift. I privately guessed that they must be recent masterpieces he had acquired from a certain company. But I was wrong. They were two new records produced by the Kaiming Company: Yan Jupeng's "Nanyang Pass" and Hu Bilan's "Fenhe Bay". Although I have two or three dozen records, my ability to distinguish them is far inferior to Zhou's. Often, I see both flaws and merits, and I am unable to be completely satisfied. Now, after listening to these two records, the sound is loud and clear, and the quality of the records is strong. Even after being played hundreds of times, there are no white scratches. They are truly the best of the best among records. So I have written this outline to inform those who share my passion and to record this brief encounter. (No payment received)

New Knowledge for the Family 115

— Compiled by Tian Xu Wo Sheng

Most of the soybean oil sold on the market is mixed with cottonseed oil. Even when the price of soybean oil and cottonseed oil are equal, it is still mixed. Cottonseed oil is extracted using lime powder, so it is extremely dry and irritating and harmful to the throat. However, there is a type of water-bleached clear oil in oil factories that is clear in quality and does not harm the throat at all, but the price is slightly higher (Yong Kang)

How to eat peanut oil: First, pour the raw oil into the pot. Cook the vegetables as usual, then pour a little raw oil around the edges of the pot. Serve immediately. When you eat it, it smells fragrant and is incredibly smooth. (Yong Kang)

During this summer season, when traveling under the hot sun, delicate faces and tender skin are often damaged by the heat. If you use Wudi brand Butterfly Cream, you can avoid this problem because it has the function of moisturizing the skin and increasing its beauty. (Zhang Mingrong)

If cooking oil is heated too much and catches fire, there is often a fire hazard. If you throw in a handful of salt, the fire in the pot will immediately go out without damaging the food. (Zhang Jinfan)

Every mealtime, flies gather, and their feet carry many germs that are left on the food. Epidemics of cholera are mostly caused by this. It is best to burn a plate of Wudi mosquito repellent incense five minutes before the meal, and all the flies will flee. (Zhao Qingpo)

If there is dust or grease on the surface of a dressing mirror or other small mirrors, do not wipe them with a wet cloth. Just wipe them with a little Wudi toothpaste and then wipe the powder off with a dry cloth. The mirror will be as bright as new. (Zhao Qingpo)

Brief Account of the Two Major Expositions in Belgium (Part 1) 116

— Six Zeng, currently residing in Paris

Belgium is a very small country. In the past, it sometimes belonged to Austria and sometimes to France. It was not until the successful revolution of 1830 that it became an independent nation. However, during the European War, it was occupied by German forces for four years. Later, with the victory of the Allied Powers, it regained its independence. This year marks the centenary of its founding. Having learned from the pain of past calamities, the Belgian people deeply appreciate the difficulty and value of independence. Therefore, the entire nation is celebrating. Special international expositions are being held in the two major cities of Liège and Antwerp, from May to November. While celebrating independence, the people can also observe the cultures of various countries and attract tourists from around the world, which will greatly benefit the country's industry and economy. This is the origin of these expositions.

Let us first discuss the Liège Exposition. Liège is one of the major industrial cities in Belgium, located at the confluence of the Meuse and Ourthe rivers. Its transportation is well-developed, and its commerce is thriving. This exposition is divided into two parts, north and south. The northern part is larger, covering an area of 140,000 square meters, located along the Meuse River. France, Italy, Japan, Poland, Switzerland, and other countries have built magnificent and beautiful pavilions here. China, on the other hand, occupies a small booth in a general pavilion jointly built by various small countries and Belgian companies and firms.

Looking at the exhibits from various countries, except for a few backward countries such as China and Egypt, most are chemical industrial products and machine-made products. There are many displays of various machines. These are the powerful tools for modern civilized countries to become rich and strong. However, China and Egypt still maintain the original state of the 15th and 16th centuries. All products are mostly made by hand. While they are exquisite, how uneconomical are they in terms of time and labor? The current difference in national strength and the distinction between civilization and barbarism depend entirely on whether a nation's people can manufacture and use machines. Therefore, one can know the state of a country's prosperity or decline by observing the exhibits at the exposition.

The Liège Exposition focuses on science and its application, large-scale industry, agriculture, and social economy (Les Scicnces et Leurs Applications' Ia Grande Industrie' I'Agriculture et I'Economie sociale). China does not have many items to display, and this time, probably due to economic reasons, it has not fully displayed them. Therefore, the content in the Chinese pavilion, which resembles an antique shop, is very poor. Silk and satin are China's only domestic products. It seems that the best quality, most colorful, and most beautiful patterns could have been collected and displayed widely. However, for some unknown reason, there were only five or six bolts of Hangzhou silk, and they were not very beautiful. On the other hand, items such as Huizhou ink and Huzhou brushes, and Chinese thread-bound books, which Westerners do not understand, were displayed in abundance, which is quite strange.

Leaving the Chinese pavilion and entering the Japanese pavilion, one's gaze immediately changes. One cannot help but admire the Japanese people's ability to handle affairs and their skill in publicity. The scale is grand, of course, but even more so, the Japanese are familiar with the Western psychology. All products are aimed at practical application. The exhibits are rich in modern colors, and the method of display conforms to scientific principles. Therefore, Westerners linger, admire, and praise without end. Silk is originally a famous product of China, but the Japanese display ten times more than us and add oil paintings of peasant women picking mulberry leaves and making cocoons, so that Westerners know the origin of silk. The same is true for embroidery and other items. In short, in addition to expressing their national characteristics, the Japanese strive to find a common ground with European society, which is to meet the needs of modern people. The Japanese have never displayed anything like Huizhou ink or Huzhou brushes, which are of no use to Westerners. The purpose of the Japanese at the exposition is not to promote antiques-style national essence but to promote international commerce.

The southern venue is smaller, and the exhibits are more educational in nature, such as municipal administration and agricultural affairs. There are many models, diagrams, and specimens on display. There is also an art museum exhibiting ancient southeastern Belgian art (I、Art Wallon Ancien). The reporter silently thought that if the Chinese pavilion were moved to the ancient art museum, it would not be much inferior.

The above is a description of the Liège Exposition. Below is a brief account of the Antwerp Exposition.

European Travelogue (68) 117

— Liu Haisu

Visiting the Palace of Versailles (3)

Yes. If China one day wants to paint this kind of historical painting, my suggestion is that while the deeds of Emperor Gaozu of Han and Emperor Taizu of Ming should be noted, the ambition of Emperor Qin Shi Huang, the genius of Emperor Yang of Sui, and the martial prowess of Genghis Khan are even more worthy of exaggeration. Originally, a strict history should take historical figures as the standard, so this French "Purple Light Pavilion" "Palace of Versailles" includes the images and deeds of wise rulers, tyrants, scholars, and poets. Let me continue our tour. Entering another hall, one immediately feels a stimulating burst of color. Hmm, it seems to be a painting by Rubens or Delacroix. Going forward to look carefully, it is indeed a large work by Delacroix. The European call Delacroix the lion of the Romantic school. He has many talents. With his strong colors and passionate expression, he single-handedly took the road that Romanticism was to take all the way to the top. Delacroix was probably the first to paint Arabs. This large mural also depicts the history of the French conquest of Morocco. The figures in the foreground have varied and strong colors. The expression of sorrowful feelings and harmonious rhythms is as moving as a drama. The oriental-style war paintings have probably reached the ultimate state of purification in this painting. Over there is another painting of the conquest of Morocco, about nine feet long. The King of Morocco, wearing yellow robes and holding a yellow umbrella, is in a state of utter disarray. Corpses are everywhere. The horror of the slaughter is depicted in great detail. We were quite moved by it. Such a massacre of a weak nation is by no means the glory of the Great French history. A picture of Napoleon's retreat from Russia. Snow covers the ground. Black and swirling clouds. The atmosphere is miserable. Napoleon rests his head on the hand of a soldier, as if this historical oddity has reached the end of his road. We also sighed in unison. A picture of Napoleon assisting Italy in the war against Austria and returning to the palace in triumph. A picture of the Franco-Dutch War in 1832. A picture of Napoleon III fighting Italy. But in the end, we feel that these paintings of spears and halberds and the horrors of the battlefield lack artistic depth. Countless war paintings were seen in various halls and cannot be recorded. This magnificent palace is a scenic spot visited by people from all over the world. Therefore, the French paint their great figures and deeds on the walls to show the glory of their history. Here, I suddenly thought of the Japanese's skill in imitation. Without anyone's effort, they vigorously imitate the Europeans in politics and academics. The forty or so murals in the so-called Meiji Shrine are like a small model of a part of the Palace of Versailles. Passing through several halls is a theater. The floor is made of marble. The decorations are elaborate. The surrounding boxes are made of five-colored marble pillars with extremely fine carvings. The proscenium is carved in stone and gilded. It is extremely beautiful. The backstage is incomparably large. Dozens of scenes are still hung on the upper part. It is said that in the time of Louis XIV, plays were performed here every day to entertain the nobles and princes. When we stepped into this theater, we immediately felt a sensual pleasure. This further made me feel that in the luxurious life of that pleasure-seeking monarch, there was the great power to promote the prosperity of art.

Financial and Gold Market in Confusion 118

Strange Changes as if in a Fog

Rapid Advances and Sharp Declines, Like a Rabbit Leaping and a Falcon Swooping

Seemingly Tending Towards Softness　Yesterday's (21st) gold market conditions were extraordinarily bizarre, rising and falling suddenly. Fluctuations of two or three taels were common, almost too fast to react to, leaving people confused and unsure. The turbulent situation saw a total difference of ten taels, revolving within five hundred and forty taels, with a tendency towards weakness. The foreign exchange market was at times divided, ultimately being mediocre, not differing greatly from the day before yesterday. Trading within the market was consistently active. Large firms like Taikang, Runyi, Yu Yuan Sheng and others largely sold off, while Xinhang, Hengxing and others actively bought in. From the start of the pre-market, due to rising silver prices, it opened low and briefly broke the thirty-tael mark. Afterwards, as buyers eagerly pursued, it immediately rose, soaring ten taels, nearly jumping to the forty-tael mark. After that, it was a case of rabbit leaps and falcon swoops, with a five or six tael pullback, unstable and unpredictable, like falling into a fog. By the afternoon, Yiyu, Yuanmao, Yong and others had resumed buying, while Taikang, Runshunli and others sold off. The exchange rate shifted from decline to equilibrium, and the market atmosphere changed from weak to firm, with a six or seven tael reversal. Subsequently, it hovered around thirty-seven taels. However, spot goods were fiery red because the market inventory was weak, so the price was very high. Timed contracts required an increase of seventeen or eighteen taels, with the potential for further increases in the future. Although large bars of silver shrank by an eighth yesterday, the silver price rose by a quarter.

However, customers wanted to bid higher for fresh goods, so japonica rice prices fluctuated slightly, but transactions were bleak. Although the Dongxin japonica rice factory wanted to push sales, buyers did not seem eager, and the trend was quiet. The general market was similar to the previous day, but there were slight differences of one or two jiao in the price fluctuations of high and lower-quality goods. New customers inquired about the source of premium rice, and the demand was still acceptable, so the market was soft. The upward trend of "Bian Yuan" (currency) was set, and buying interest was also flat, so the market was firm.

Hu'nan: Few shipments arrived from river routes. Street sales did not expand due to the scarcity of goods. Regular broken japonica rice was scarce and little traded. Although Sutong japonica rice slightly met market demand, the overall atmosphere was lackluster. Southern short-grain rice arrivals and sales were minimal, and prices were stable. Top-quality goods remained at 21 yuan. White Yuan rice was extremely scarce here, and there were slight inquiries about hanging sales, and the market was holding steady.

Foreign Rice Amidst the Lifting of the Ban on Hunan Rice 128

Yesterday, foreign rice still did not see large-scale sales, and the market remained sluggish. Furthermore, the scheduled lifting of the ban on Hunan rice has become a reality, and it has been reported that the ban will be lifted on September 1st, with a quota of 5 million bags, and a fee of 5 yuan per bag will be charged. Although rice inventories in Shanghai are low, sales have been stagnant for a long time, and the market has been weak. If this large batch of Hunan rice comes to Shanghai, the market will definitely be greatly affected. However, there are still questions: can Hunan rice be shipped out in quantities of 5 million? Will this number be shipped to Shanghai in full? After adding passport fees and all miscellaneous taxes and transportation costs, will it be profitable to trade? Therefore, the rice market in Shanghai has not yet experienced major fluctuations, only suspicion and fear, and buyers are taking a wait-and-see approach. Saigon No. 1 rice has a relatively large inventory in Shanghai, and sales are slow. Yesterday, due to the news of the lifting of the ban on Hunan rice, the market price immediately fell by 3 jiao. Other types of rice fell by small fractions ranging from a few cents to one jiao. A total of 200 bags of No. 1 Saigon rice were sold, priced at 16 yuan to 16 yuan and 3 jiao; 750 bags of Andong Geng, priced at 16 yuan and 5 jiao and 7 fen; 500 bags of Da Wen, priced at 12 yuan and 3 jiao and a half to 3 jiao; and 300 bags of Min Dang, priced at 14 yuan and 9 jiao to 3 jiao and 7 fen.

Flour Market Shows Slight Improvement in Evening Session 129

Tianjin Flood May Affect Inventories

After the flour market opened yesterday morning, the market for each month remained very quiet, so although the quoted price of foreign wheat recovered by 4 or 5 jiao, sentiment was still not very good. However, the market atmosphere this month has been stronger. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, it was still stable. Suddenly, news came that Tianjin was flooded and the autumn grain crop may be affected, so sentiment suddenly rose, and buying interest in both near and far-term contracts suddenly increased, and was better than the previous day by 1 fen. Looking at the future of the flour market, the biggest problem is that the factories must release chips before there can be a larger loosening. This month is already at a standstill, and no matter what, it will be difficult to fall below the 5 qian mark again. As a result, August and September each rose 1 fen, October, December and January rose 1 fen and 2.5 li, and November rose 1 fen and a half.

Wheat Market Firm 130

After the wheat futures market opened yesterday, the prices for each month fluctuated and then tended to be firm, because the quoted price of foreign wheat was slightly better, and this month, due to the large bullish positions, prices have been maintained. Because the value is too low, there are preparations to receive the goods, otherwise, there is still consideration of gradually settling. As a result, August, November, and December remained unchanged, September was up 1 fen, and December was up 2 fen. Because the factories unanimously maintained high prices for spot wheat, there was no trading in wheat arriving by ship or cart from various routes. The entire market only saw 150 bags of Xiashi ship wheat traded at a price of 4 taels, 7 qian, and 7 fen.

Silk and Tea Market Downturn Continues 131

Since the Assistance Association stopped handling Gongxi tea, the tea market has undergone major changes. British and French tea merchants are taking the opportunity to depress prices for various green teas from both road and local estates, and the acceptance of bids is becoming increasingly stringent. The ability of Chinese tea merchants to resist this situation has also weakened. Yesterday, the market price for Zhenmei tea fell by another 5 taels, and transactions were scarce, sentiment was weak, and the overall trend was declining. However, although the Russian merchants arrested in Hankou have not yet been released, the central government still allows the Russian firms to continue protecting tea production, which may offer some relief, and the Russian estates still have hope of reopening.

Sugar Market: Meiji Sugar Suddenly Opens with 20,000 Bags 132

Raw and White Sugar Market Turns Quiet

Yesterday's sugar market saw dispatches from the producing region. The current price of Cuban sugar was 1.15625, a decrease of 0.03125 compared to the previous dispatch. The price of New York sugar futures for September was 1.12, December 1.21, March of next year 1.32, and May 1.40, each down 1 cent compared to the previous dispatch, except for December, which was down 2 cents. Spot and futures prices for Java sugar remained unchanged. Buying interest in raw and white sugar from the association was scarce, and sellers rushed to sell, with bids at 7 taels and 9 qian and a half, but no one inquired. As a result, there were no transactions in the entire city. Finely ground white sugar was at 8 taels and 2 fen and a half, and buying and selling were also sluggish. With the easing of factory bids for Japanese sugar, Meiji factory sugar suddenly opened with 20,000 bags for October and November delivery, priced at 4 yuan and 8 jiao in Japanese currency, which was 2 jiao cheaper than Dali sugar. And because the Eastern exchange rate has recently become cheaper, merchants have been eager to buy, and sales were quickly completed. However, the atmosphere in the spot market for drawn sugar has been slightly dampened, and transactions are scarce. TY mark was at 7 taels, 7 qian, and 7 fen and a half, N mark was at 7 taels and 8 qian and 7 fen and a half, and no other marks were traded.

Dried Fruit Market: New Honey Dates Prices Have Eased 133

Since new Jiaxing honey dates appeared on the market, the supply has gradually increased, and prices have eased. The initial batch was once sold for 28 taels, but yesterday's transactions on the market streets saw sales at 25 taels, a decrease of 3 taels. Up and down gears still follow the usual practice of adding and subtracting. The market outlook is flat. Old stock, because most of the sugar juice has melted, is very weak even though it is cheap.

Black Pepper Plummets by 15 Taels 134

Public Market Difficult to Maintain

Previously, due to the sharp drop in production prices and the lack of customer sales, the black pepper market plummeted, heading downstream every day. Trading houses opened at 75 taels and gradually fell to below 50 taels. Later, because the losses were too heavy, the trading houses mutually agreed to establish a public market to maintain the market and protect costs. Therefore, the market price was able to rebound to between 57 and 58 taels. However, customer sales remain stagnant, supply exceeds demand, inventories are increasing daily, and foreign firm goods are flooding the market, making it difficult to maintain the public market. The market then fell sharply. Yesterday, Nisshin Yoko opened for sale 150 bags of No. 1 pepper at a price of 43 taels and a half. Merchants' interest was extremely weak, and it is said that less than half of the goods were sold. The weakness of the market has reached an extreme point. Compared to the market price last week, the price has fallen by 14 or 15 taels, and the intensity of the decline is unprecedented.

Various Circles in This City Telegraph the National Government to Thoroughly Eliminate Reactionaries 156

Destroy the Rebel Nests in the North...Clear Out the Communist Lairs in the South

Clarify the Universe...Relieve the People from Suffering

—Telegram from the Memorial Service for Liao Zhongkai’s Martyrdom—

At the fifth anniversary memorial service for Liao Zhongkai's martyrdom the other day, two major resolutions were passed by various circles in this city: (1) To send a special telegram to comfort the soldiers fighting against the rebellion in the front lines; (2) To telegraph the National Government to thoroughly eliminate all reactionary forces, comforting the soldiers fighting against the rebellion in the front lines. The telegram has already been seen in yesterday's newspaper. Now we will explore the telegram to the National Government as follows: To the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, forwarded to the National Government: Having repeatedly read the triumphant reports, we are delighted to learn that Tai'an and Jinan have been successively recovered. The main force of the rebellious Yan has been almost completely lost, and the remnant troops of the rebellious Feng are terrified upon hearing the news. Sweeping away the enemy's lair and destroying their base is just around the corner. All these achievements are due to the soldiers in the front lines who are determined to dedicate their lives. However, it also relies on the planning of Liao Zhongkai while Dr. Sun Yat-sen was in Japan, and the training of a party army with principles. Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek was also able to lead the party army to successively eliminate reactionary forces. However, the martyr Mr. Liao had not fulfilled his long-cherished wish and suffered the harm of villains. The future of the party and the country suddenly lost a mentor, and the responsibility of our comrades became even heavier. On this fifth anniversary of Mr. Liao's martyrdom for the party and the country, imperialists are still creating rumors and causing trouble, warlord reactionaries are still jumping and causing trouble in Hebei, and communist traitors are lurking in various places, recklessly engaging in sabotage to prolong the lives of feudal warlords at the cost of flattering Soviet rubles. Our Central Government should remember Mr. Liao's revolutionary love, and at this critical moment, it is even more important to eliminate the root of the disaster, taking advantage of the pursuit of fleeing enemies and the accumulated power. When the reactionary elements are frightened, quickly send a large army to thoroughly eliminate all reactionary remnants, destroy the rebel nests in the north, sweep away the communist lairs in the south, clarify the universe, and relieve the people from suffering, so that we can report to the Dr. Sun Yat-sen and the spirits of the martyrs in heaven without guilt, and rebuild the process of political tutelage and construction. As the telegram rushes forward, we eagerly await the triumph.

Chairman Wang of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Took Office Yesterday 157

Delivering a Speech on Assuming Office

Since the election of Wang Xiaoce as the successor to the chairmanship of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce by the executive committee at a special meeting the other day, all executive and supervisory committee members immediately urged Chairman Wang to take office to emphasize the importance of chamber affairs. At that time, Wang expressed that he still needed to consider it. Yesterday at noon, all standing committee members went to the chamber and strongly urged Wang to take office again. Wang then immediately promised to take the position. He stamped the report on the re-election and took the chair at the standing committee meeting. At the same time, Mr. Xu Jiting also respected the resolution of the executive committee's special meeting and went to the chamber yesterday to take up the position of standing committee member. The report to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, the Municipal Party Headquarters, and your letter, as well as the speech delivered by Chairman Wang, are summarized as follows.

Report to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs and the Municipal Party Headquarters: The subordinate chamber's chairman, Committee Member Xu Jiting, repeatedly requested to resign, and it was impossible to retain him. It has been resolved by the executive committee to elect another person to emphasize the importance of chamber affairs. Furthermore, on the 20th of this month, Wang Xiaoce was elected as chairman and committee member, and we report for your examination and approval, requesting your preservation and transfer for record. The case is that the subordinate chamber's chairman, Committee Member Xu Jiting, immediately declared his resignation after being legally elected by the executive committee on July 1st, and has not attended chamber affairs since then. Subsequently, the executive committee resolved to retain him at two special executive committee meetings on July 3rd and July 10th and went to persuade him in person. He only took office on the 17th, and on the same day, he submitted a report to your bureau requesting sick leave due to busy affairs and long-term insomnia. The duties were temporarily assumed by the four standing committee members Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Yuan Ludeng, and Ye Huijun. On the 7th of this month, he again requested to resign and elect another person because his health had not yet recovered and he could not bear the heavy burden. Although the subordinate chamber's third executive committee meeting resolved to request him to maintain the resolutions of the two special executive committee meetings on July 3rd and July 10th, he still sent a letter firmly requesting resignation. Examining the situation, there was no way to reverse the trend. On the 20th of this month, a special executive committee meeting was convened to resolve the matter. On that day, ten executive committee members attended, and all agreed that the chairman's handling of chamber affairs was a very important responsibility. Since he had already firmly resigned and could not be retained, another person should be elected in accordance with the law to emphasize the importance of chamber affairs. It was resolved that the election would be held immediately among the current standing committee members in accordance with the law. As a result of the election, Wang Xiaolai was elected with nine votes. It was also resolved to send a letter to Xu Jiting requesting him to attend the position of standing committee member as soon as his illness improved to jointly participate in chamber affairs. All the reasons for the firm request for resignation by the subordinate chamber's chairman, Committee Member Xu Jiting, and the supplementary election of Wang Xiaoce in accordance with the law, are hereby prepared and reported, requesting your bureau's examination and approval, and requesting you to forward the report for record, which would be a public convenience.

To Standing Committee Member Xu Jiting: In response to your letter received on the 11th of this month, regarding the third executive committee's resolution to retain you, you still strongly requested to fulfill the agreement to re-elect. A special executive committee meeting was convened on the 20th of this month to discuss the matter. It was resolved that since you had firmly resigned, the only option was to elect another person in accordance with the law. Standing Committee Member Wang Xiaolai has been elected as chairman and committee member to take over. Furthermore, your letter of the 7th of this month originally stated that you would take the position of standing committee member as soon as your health improved. You should be requested to come to the chamber to take the position of standing committee member as soon as your health improves so that you can jointly participate in chamber affairs. Accordingly, the case is recorded and communicated to you, and I hope you will investigate and acknowledge it.

Speech by Chairman Wang Xiaolai: Chairman Wang said to the reporter of Xinsheng News Agency: Mr. Xu Jiting was recently elected as the chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and everyone celebrated the acquisition of a talented person. However, Mr. Xu firmly resigned due to illness. The entire committee of the chamber jointly persuaded him to stay, but he did not agree. The executive committee then elected me to take his place. I have always had a desire to serve society, so when it comes to social affairs, I dare not refuse any assignment. However, I am still very cautious about public appointments and only take them after careful consideration. Even in recent years, when I have assisted in tax collection, it was because I had some knowledge of business conditions and hoped to alleviate the difficulties faced by merchants in Jiangsu as my duty. If I am capable, I will definitely fulfill my duty. If I see difficulties and shirk responsibility or pursue my own interests, then it would not be the foolish and honest nature that I dare to pretend to be. Now, as I take office as the chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, I must say that the position is complex and the responsibilities are heavy, and I am not capable of handling them. Moreover, Mr. Xu is highly respected, yet he modestly declined. How dare I not assess my own abilities and rashly take office? However, considering that the issue of the chairman of the chamber of commerce has been delayed for a long time and has not been resolved, I am fortunate that the standing committee members have taken responsibility for maintaining it, so that it has not been suspended. However, if the issue of the chairman is not resolved as soon as possible, then the organization of the chamber will not be completed, and how can we plan for progress? At this time, the chamber will be given an unnecessary ridicule and unfavorable speculation. Considering my sincere spirit of striving for revolution and my long-cherished desire to serve society, I cannot allow my personal situation to cause any obstacles. After careful consideration, I wanted to imitate Mr. Xu's high-mindedness, but it was impossible. I had no choice but to take on the difficult task and do my best. If I rely on the guidance and assistance of all the executive and supervisory committee members and the standing committee members, so that the chamber affairs can flourish day by day, if there comes a time when I cannot fulfill my responsibilities, then I will follow the precedent of Chairman Xu and report the situation and request the standing committee members to elect another wise and capable person to emphasize the importance of chamber affairs. At this point, Chairman Wang had other business to attend to, so the reporter bid farewell. The long-delayed issue of the chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has come to an end.

Minutes of the Standing Committee Meeting: The eighth standing committee meeting was held at 1:00 PM yesterday. The committee members present were Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Yuan Ludeng, Luo Qinghua, etc. (1) Conducted formalities as usual. (2) Read and approved the resolutions of the seventh standing committee meeting. (3) Discussed the report of the Labor-Management Issues Research Committee on the review of the reasons for the Chinese Medicine Industry's request to modify the conditions, requesting approval. Resolved: Forward as is. (4) Discussed the referral from the Commerce Department requesting a review of the application of Zhenghua Silver Company for membership. Resolved: Approve membership. (5) Discussed the referral from the General Affairs Department requesting an investigation of the accounts of the goods commissioned by the Qingdao National Products Exhibition Hall for display at the chamber. Resolved: Send the remaining funds from the accounts to the Qingdao National Products Exhibition Hall to clear the procedures. (6) Discussed the cases of securing guarantors for various important staff members. Resolved: Approved separately.

City Chamber of Commerce Discusses Developing Trade with India 158

Plans to Organize a Chinese Products Exhibition in India

The City Chamber of Commerce's National Goods Promotion Committee convened a meeting on the 20th of this month regarding the promotion of national goods and foreign trade in response to the Indian boycott of British goods. Representatives from various national goods industries and members of the National Goods Promotion Committee were invited. Over thirty people attended, including Shen Huachen from the silk industry, Zhu Chunbo from the electrical machinery industry, Shen Shuyu from the silk weaving industry, Shen Ziyang from the mercerized cotton weaving industry, Cheng Guichu from the cotton cloth industry, Shen Tianxin, Chen Liangyu, Jin Chuxiang, and others. The chairman, Lu Wenshao, first reported on the situation, followed by representatives from various industries and committee members who expressed their opinions. They all agreed that the Indian boycott of British goods was an excellent opportunity to promote national goods and foreign trade, and that a concrete organization should be established to handle the matter. The following resolutions were passed: (1) Collect samples from various national goods factories, send personnel to India to hold an exhibition, and select personnel to conduct on-site investigations. (2) Publicly recommend Zhu Chunbo, Lu Wenshao, Shen Shuyu, and Lin Zimao to draft the organizational outline of the exhibition and name it the "Chinese Products Exhibition in India." (3) After drafting the exhibition outline, it must be submitted to the National Goods Promotion Committee for review and approval before formulating a plan and convening a discussion with various national goods factories regarding the implementation procedures. (4) Find out the current tax laws in India to use as a reference. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Municipal Party Headquarters Requests Central Government to Reorganize Shanghai Republic Daily 160

According to Guominshe, the Shanghai Republic Daily, is a Chinese Nationalist Party newspaper with a long history in Shanghai. Recently, the Municipal Party Headquarters requested the Central Party Headquarters to send personnel to reorganize the newspaper, citing its abnormal attitude, strange behavior, and disregard for Party Headquarters news, in order to rectify it. The original submission is recorded below:

Submission to the Central Government: Regarding the Shanghai Republic Daily's recent strange behavior, reversed news, and disregard for Party Headquarters news, which hinders the Party's propaganda, we request your review, dispatch of personnel for reorganization, and promotion of propaganda. The Republic Daily is the only Party newspaper in the city, and all news related to Party affairs in the city is published by the Republic Daily. Therefore, the Party Headquarters has high hopes for the newspaper, and the newspaper bears a heavy responsibility. However, the newspaper's recent behavior has been strange, the news has been reversed, the Party Headquarters' news has been disregarded, and the Party's propaganda has been hindered. The facts are listed as follows: (1) The Propaganda Department's fifteenth municipal propaganda meeting was based on the Central Party's order to discuss the expansion of the anti-communist movement. The resolutions were sent to various newspapers for publication. Xinwen Bao, Shishi Xinbao, and others, seeing the importance of the news, published it on the front page of the local news section. However, the Republic Daily, which is guided by the Headquarters, published it in the Party affairs column after the branch news and altered it without permission, adding arbitrary titles. This is a small matter of lacking basic editing knowledge, but a major matter of disregarding important Party affairs news and delaying the Party's propaganda. (2) The memorial of Mr. Liao Zhongkai's martyrdom was one of the important revolutionary memorial days for the Party. The Propaganda Department published the propaganda points in the local news section of various newspapers. Shen Xin and other major newspapers published it on the front page because Mr. Liao was an advanced member of the Party and the country and a revolutionary martyr, which was very eye-catching. However, the Republic Daily, which receives subsidies from the Party and is guided by the Headquarters, published it at the end of the Party affairs column, reversing the importance of things. Based on the above facts, the Headquarters believes that the Republic Daily's actions not only hinder propaganda but also cause misunderstandings to the outside world. Therefore, we submit this document, along with newspaper clippings, and request your review and prompt dispatch of personnel for reorganization to promote propaganda. This will benefit the Party. Respectfully submitted to the Central Executive Committee.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Determined the Scope of the Jinliyuan Case Arbitration 164

Arbitrator Certificates Have Been Issued

According to Xinsheng News Agency, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has hired lawyer Gao Shuo as an arbitrator for the Jinliyuan Wharf case. Yesterday, General Manager Cai, based on the results of the meeting of important personnel of the company (the 20th) the day before, personally presented the arbitrator certificate to lawyer Gao, along with the scope of the arbitrator's authority and the range of rent valuation and payment guarantee. However, as of last night, the Trinitarian Church has not yet given a formal response.

According to Guowen News Agency, the dispute between the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jinliyuan Wharf and the French Catholic Trinitarian Church lease has changed from legal procedures to arbitration. Yesterday, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company issued a full power of attorney to lawyer Gao Shuo, stating the scope of rent increase and term limit, and requested him to handle the matter within that scope. Currently, Mr. Gao is waiting for notification from the Trinitarian Church. Once the church appoints an arbitrator, the two parties can formally meet and proceed. Yesterday, Mr. Gao also visited people in the church, such as Ma Xiangbo and Lu Bohong, asking them to help. It is said that when the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Trinitarian Church first signed the contract in the early years of Guangxu, it was handled by Ma Xiangbo's younger brother, Ma Meishu (who was then the general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company). Therefore, Ma Xiangbo is especially willing to mediate.

Intense Competition in Sino-American Shipping 165

A Total of 112 Merchant Ships from Four Countries

Resulting in More Ships Than Cargo and Excess Tonnage

This year, the competition among shipping companies of various countries on the Sino-American route for the transportation of Chinese export goods is unprecedented. The shipping merchants of Britain, Japan, and the United States are especially engaged in head-to-head competition. The recent situation of intense competition is recorded below:

Arrival of New Ships Continued: After Nippon Yusen Kaisha (NYK) added six fast ships in the Pacific, Osaka Shosen Kaisha (OSK) followed suit by building six strong, fast, and large ships. British company Jardine Matheson specially built the unprecedentedly large ship, the Empress of Japan. Two large ships built by American company American Mail Line will also be completed soon, with one expected to be finished first. NYK's fifth new ship, the Hie Maru, a sister ship of the Hikawa Maru, is scheduled to begin its maiden voyage tomorrow. The second new ship of the Daiban, the Tokai Maru, is also being rushed to completion. According to a telegram received yesterday, it will arrive in Shanghai on the 24th and begin its maiden voyage to the United States on the 26th. British company Butterfield & Swire's New York liner has also switched to using the motor vessel Lyell City. The total number of ships newly added to the Sino-American route this year is 23, with an estimated total tonnage of 300,000 tons.

Intense Business Competition: After the new ships started service, they competed by boasting about their fast sailing speed. The competition for transporting Chinese export goods, especially silk and tea, was particularly fierce, resulting in no hope of price increases. For miscellaneous goods that are not abundant, prices were lowered to compete for cargo. For example, sesame seeds were reduced from four yuan per ton to two yuan and fifty cents. Other goods were reduced by 30%. This is the opposite of the increased freight rates on the European route after the gold standard was raised. Recently, shipping companies on the Sino-American route have been secretly lowering freight rates after the price cuts. Due to excessive competition, they are jealous of each other. All cargo freight rates and cargo manifests are prohibited from being leaked. If staff members reveal the true situation of freight rates and export goods, they will be fined 1,000 yuan. Inquiries from competitors are even more suspected. This action imitates that action. Today, the Sino-American freight industry has become a deeply secretive situation.

More Ships Than Cargo: The number of ships on the Sino-American route is increasing daily, while the number of goods is decreasing daily. (1) Due to the obstruction of transportation in the Chinese interior and the impact of the current situation, export trade is sluggish. (2) An unlimited number of ships are competing to transport a limited amount of cargo, naturally resulting in excess tonnage. In the past, only one ship sailed from Shanghai to New York every week. Now, it has increased to five ships. On the San Francisco-Seattle route, which used to have only two ships, it has now increased to four ships, resulting in the current situation of more ships than cargo. Even if prices are lowered, there is no cargo to transport. Therefore, almost all Sino-American liners have suffered losses this year. If this competition continues, the Sino-American shipping industry

Page 14

will inevitably lead to mutual bankruptcy.

Current Shipping Lines: Currently, the ships sailing on the Sino-American route are from four countries: Britain, the United States, Japan, and Norway. Analyzing the count: (A) Japanese companies include NYK's 12 Pacific liners, 6 New York liners, OSK's 6 Pacific ships, 6 New York ships, and Kawasaki's 6 ships. (B) The United States includes American Mail Line's 6 New York ships, 9 Pacific ships, and Dollar Steamship Lines' 6 ships. (C) British companies include Jardine Matheson's 4 Pacific ships, Prince Line's 6 New York ships, China Navigation Company's 6 ships, and Blue Funnel Line and Butterfield & Swire's 4 ships each. (D) Norwegian companies include Fearnley & Eger's 3 ships and Barber Line's 6 ships. In addition, the British ships represented by Jardine Matheson include 28 ships sailing in the Pacific. The above are all regular liners, totaling 112 ships, with a total tonnage of over 1 million tons, which is quite alarming.

No Changes to the Sino-German Aviation Agreement 166

Ratification Documents Can Be Sent Out Within Two or Three Days

The Sino-German aviation contract, officially signed in Beijing by Wang Boqun, Minister of Communications and Plenipotentiary Representative of China, and Schmidt, Plenipotentiary Representative of Germany, has been over five months. It is only awaiting formal ratification to take effect. Yesterday, according to a Beijing report, there were rumors of changes. A reporter from Xinsheng News Agency visited German consultant Fuchsel and Chinese consultant lawyer Liu Shifang yesterday. According to lawyer Liu, the rumors of changes are absolutely incorrect. The ratification documents were originally scheduled to be issued on the 16th. Lawyer Liu himself was originally scheduled to go to Qingdao with German representative Schmidt on the 16th. On the morning of that day, when boarding the ship, lawyer Liu planned to hand over the ratification documents to Schmidt for signature and delivery to the Ministry. However, lawyer Liu suddenly fell ill, so he could not sign and send them out as scheduled. Now, the ratification documents have been sent to Qingdao by lawyer Liu three days ago to be signed by Schmidt and can be sent to the Ministry of Communications in Shanghai within two or three days. The rumors of changes are not true.

City Chamber of Commerce Inquires About Huludao Port Affairs 167

The City Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Huludao Port Authority of Liaoning yesterday, stating that according to a letter from the Italian Postal Shipping Company, there were five questions regarding Huludao: (1) Is there a safe location to berth foreign import ships? (2) What is the depth of the draft? (3) Are there any taxes and fees required for entering the port? (4) Can the port allow foreign giant ships to enter at any time, or is it only possible during the daytime? (5) For building materials, such as cement, are there barges or other ships available to transport the goods from the barges to the shore? Please provide instructions for reply.

Northern Majia Section Telephone Line Accepted Yesterday 168

The telephone project from North Bridge to Majia Bridge in Shanghai County was completed at the beginning of this month. The County Construction Bureau reported to the Jiangsu Construction Department, requesting personnel to accept it. The Department appointed Li Zhen, assistant engineer of the Jiangsu Electrical Industry Management Office, to come to Shanghai for acceptance. First, the telephone sound was tested, followed by Bureau Chief and others walking along the road to inspect the electrical pole line project until Majia Bridge. Committee Member Li believed that the telephone sound and the project were both perfect. It is a pity that the route is too short. All districts in Puxi must be laid out in a unified manner to facilitate local news and achieve significant results. After the inspection, they returned to Shanghai in the original car. Committee Member Li then said goodbye and returned to the province to report.

Social Bureau Orders Investigation into Truth of Rising Flour and Wheat Prices 169

Recently, the flour and wheat market has shown signs of cornering again. It is said that a small number of people are manipulating it. After receiving the news, the Municipal Social Bureau believed that the period between the old and new harvests has not yet passed. Rising flour and wheat prices will inevitably endanger the people's food. The market prices are all in a backwardation situation. At this time when new wheat is on the market, this should not be the case. It is also heard that two brokers in the Grain Exchange have purchased and stored too much. The Bureau has ordered both the Flour Exchange and the Wheat Exchange to find ways to stabilize prices and set a deadline for investigation and reporting.

Meeting Record of the Inland Flour Mill Association 171

The Inland Flour Mill Association of this port is the organization for the inland flour mill operators in the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui. It held an emergency meeting the day before yesterday. It is heard that the content of the proposal is to express disapproval of the new Jiangbei branch of the Shanghai Agricultural Product Inspection Institute of the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining, which intends to inspect wheat and charge fees, causing disturbances. It also proposed that the inland factories' flour be added to the exchange's standards. It is heard that the regulations set by the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining Inspection Institute this time are quite strict. A branch is set up in the Jiangbei area for inspection. A fee of one point per stone of wheat is charged. The Association argues that the Ministry of Agriculture's inspection of wheat is a good intention to improve agricultural products and has nothing to do with flour mills. It should only be applied to farmers and not to factories. Because the factory operators will never buy impurities, and the fee of one point is like extracting wheat tax. Moreover, if the wheat quality is found to be problematic in the middle of the transportation from the northern provinces, how will it be handled? Now, the inspection is not carried out simultaneously in all provinces, but only in Jiangbei, Jiangsu, which makes the Jiangsu factory operators suffer bullying. Therefore, it was decided to send a letter to the Institute to state this intention. As for joining the exchange standards, because the Shanghai Flour Exchange is the trading market for Chinese machine-made flour and has been established for many years, the flour factories in Shanghai and Wuxi have already joined the standards of the exchange and can trade freely. However, the inland factories have not yet joined, which makes it difficult to transport flour to Shanghai for sale. This time, it was decided to send a letter to the Institute requesting to join the standards.

Labor Unrest in the Nihua Cotton Mill 178

The Factory is Plotting to Start Work

The Labor Side is Preparing to Respond

According to Guominshe News Agency, the labor unrest in the Nihua Cotton Mill in Pudong has lasted for more than a month. The factory has announced the closure and opening of the factory twice. Recently, there has been news of using a large sum of money to persuade workers to resume work. The cunning of the Japanese businessmen can be seen in general here. The situation is explored as follows:

Using a Large Sum of Money to Bribe Lackeys: Since the factory strike has lasted for more than a month, the factory has not only not realized its mistakes, but has also been engaged in cruel destruction. According to reliable information from the union, the Japanese in the factory used 8,000 yuan to bribe six lackeys to discuss ways to start work in a certain place in Hongkou.

Hiring Thugs to Beat People: It is heard that the lackeys, after discussing the results this time, hired 100 thugs, giving each person ten yuan per worker, specializing in beating the leaders of the workers and the members of the Workers' Consolidation Committee, and at the same time rushing to the workers' residences to intimidate the workers to go to work unconditionally.

Workers' Consolidation Committee Meets to Deal with It: The Workers' Consolidation Committee of the factory, considering that the strike has been going on for a long time, in order to properly maintain the lives of the workers, decided at yesterday's meeting that, starting from today, in addition to inviting various unions in Pudong to discuss ways to deal with the situation, they will also send people to various unions in Puxi to contact the organization of a support association. In addition, there are many resolutions, but the content will not be announced for the time being. It is also heard that they are making great efforts to raise relief funds. Account books and donation registers are all prepared. Once the Municipal Party Headquarters approves, they can start working.

The Communist Party's Plan Did Not Succeed: After the factory strike, the Communist Party tried to seize control and manipulate it from the middle, spreading various rumors and conveying them to the party and government organs. Later, because the workers were unwilling to be fooled, and at the same time the party and government organs came out to advocate justice, the workers all abided by the guidance and waited quietly for mediation. The Communist Party, seeing that one plan did not succeed, retreated and colluded with the lackeys, hoping to cause trouble and destruction, inducing the workers to go to work unconditionally. On the one hand, they spread rumors again, blaming the party and government organs. How poisonous is the Communist Party. It is a pity that people have already seen through their treachery, and the party and government organs have also made great efforts for this matter. Although the Communist Party is cunning, their plan will definitely not succeed.

Negotiations on Cases of Cross-Border Investigation by the Municipal Council 181

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted a petition to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau requesting negotiations regarding cases of cross-border investigation by the Municipal Council. The original petition stated, "On the 6th of this month, we received a letter from the Rickshaw Guild stating that on the 2nd of this month, at 8:00 AM, individuals claiming to be detectives Wang Chengying and Feng Zhiming from the Fourth Avenue Police Station of the Public Concession Municipal Council came to the Nanshi Guild Hall (i.e., the Jianghuai Native Place Association outside the Great South Gate) to inquire about the identities of Wang Rongqing, Zhang Huaiyang, and Zhang Shizhou. Our association secretary, Zhang Shizhou, led them to a secluded room for a detailed discussion. The detectives stated that someone had recently accused them to the Fourth Avenue Police Station of being disorderly elements. The police station, for the sake of prudence, had come to conduct an on-site investigation. They suggested that the reason for the accusation and its contents be inquired directly from Detective Chief Lu Liankui at the police station. Subsequently, after committee members Da Jin and Ding Lianyuan informed them about the reorganization process and internal situation, the detectives copied down the detailed addresses of Wang Rongqing and others and left. Upon hearing this, our association was deeply alarmed, considering it to be a fabricated accusation. Even if the law were effective, it would still be subject to suppression. Since the police station belongs to the concession, it has no right to accept accusations or send personnel for investigation. We request you to swiftly negotiate with the Public Concession based on reason to protect human rights and warn against future occurrences." The letter arrived at the association after the Rickshaw Guild had been requested to provide the addresses of the three persons and confirm whether they lived in the concession or the Chinese territory, since their address was located in Chinese territory. Now, we have received a reply stating that Wang Rongqing resides at No. 126, Santai Wharf, Lianghui Street, Nanshi; Zhang Huaiyang resides at No. 28, Darenli, east end of Xie Bridge; and Zhang Shizhou resides at No. 4, Lirenli, Limalu, South Pier. Considering the above circumstances, all the accused individuals in this case have their offices and private residences outside the concession. The Municipal Council's police station should not have accepted the case across borders or dispatched detectives for investigation. This matter concerns the infringement of the Chinese government's administrative authority. We reasonably submit this situation to your bureau for review to determine whether or not to forward it to the municipal government for strict negotiations. Awaiting your decision."

Three Notices from the Jinghu and Huhangyong Railway Transportation Departments 183

Implement Safety Measures for Train Accidents

Restrictions on Transporting Goods by Train

Train Arrivals and Departures Require Telegraph Notifications

The Transportation Department of the Jinghu (Nanjing-Shanghai) and Huhangyong (Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo) Railways yesterday issued three notices to station staff: (1) Recent investigations have revealed that accidental events are often not reported, or the safety measures stipulated in the "Regulations for Train Accident Rescue" are not followed, or the personnel are completely unaware of the relevant regulations, which is highly inappropriate. In the future, any incidents must be reported immediately, and the regulations outlined in the "Regulations for Train Accident Rescue" must be strictly followed. Any deliberate violations will be punished. (2) Only railway cars that are in good condition and sturdy are permitted to transport goods on the Jinghu Line. When transporting lumber, only steel cars from the Jinghu Line must be used. Due to incomplete mechanical equipment, the 10-ton freight cars of this line, whether boxcars or livestock cars, are not allowed to transport goods to the Jinghu Line. Please pay attention. (3) The head of the Hangzhou Transportation Section reported that it has been found that when trains arrive or depart from a station, the stationmaster sends a telegram to the preceding or following station for the sake of train safety, which is of utmost importance. However, stations are treating this as a mere formality and not following the regulations, either using a telephone for notification or inquiring by telephone afterwards to fill in the information. This disregards the importance of safe train operation. Despite repeated warnings, this habit is difficult to change. It is requested that each station be ordered to cut out, sign, and submit the telegram strips of train arrival and departure times daily to the relevant section chief for verification. A telegraph operator should be specially assigned by the section chief to review the telegram strips to see if they comply with the regulations. If this is done, there will be no excuse. Please advise whether this is feasible. Based on this report, it has been found that stationmasters are not following the regulations for notifying the preceding and following stations by telegram when trains arrive or depart, which is not in accordance with train safety. Therefore, we hereby send a circular to inform and admonish each stationmaster to cut out and sign the telegram strips of train arrival and departure times, starting from today, and submit them to the respective section chiefs for verification.
